<p><b>John Ono Lennon</b>, <span style="font-size:85%;"><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Member_of_the_Order_of_the_British_Empire" title="Member of the Order of the British Empire">MBE</a></span>, born <b>John Winston Lennon</b>; (9 October 1940 – 8 December 1980), was an English musician, singer and songwriter who rose to worldwide fame as a founder member of the rock band <a href="/wiki/The_Beatles" title="The Beatles">the Beatles</a>, the most commercially successful band in the history of popular music. With <a href="/wiki/Paul_McCartney" title="Paul McCartney">Paul McCartney</a>, he formed a <a href="/wiki/Lennon%E2%80%93McCartney" title="Lennon–McCartney">songwriting partnership</a> that is one of the most celebrated of the 20th century.</p>
<p>Born and raised in <a href="/wiki/Liverpool" title="Liverpool">Liverpool</a>, as a teenager Lennon became involved in the <a href="/wiki/Skiffle#Skiffle_in_Britain" title="Skiffle">skiffle craze</a>; his first band, <a href="/wiki/The_Quarrymen" title="The Quarrymen">the Quarrymen</a>, evolved into the Beatles in 1960. When <a href="/wiki/Break-up_of_the_Beatles" title="Break-up of the Beatles">the group disbanded</a> in 1970, Lennon embarked on a solo career that produced the critically acclaimed albums <i><a href="/wiki/John_Lennon/Plastic_Ono_Band" title="John Lennon/Plastic Ono Band">John Lennon/Plastic Ono Band</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Imagine_(John_Lennon_album)" title="Imagine (John Lennon album)">Imagine</a></i>, and iconic songs such as "<a href="/wiki/Give_Peace_a_Chance" title="Give Peace a Chance">Give Peace a Chance</a>" and "<a href="/wiki/Working_Class_Hero" title="Working Class Hero">Working Class Hero</a>". After his marriage to <a href="/wiki/Yoko_Ono" title="Yoko Ono">Yoko Ono</a> in 1969, he changed his name to John Ono Lennon. Lennon disengaged himself from the music business in 1975 to raise his infant son <a href="/wiki/Sean_Lennon" title="Sean Lennon">Sean</a>, but re-emerged with Ono in 1980 with the new album <i><a href="/wiki/Double_Fantasy" title="Double Fantasy">Double Fantasy</a></i>. He was <a href="/wiki/Death_of_John_Lennon" title="Death of John Lennon">murdered</a> three weeks after its release.</p>
<p>Lennon revealed a rebellious nature and acerbic wit in his music, writing, drawings, on film and in interviews. Controversial through his political and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Peace_activist" title="Peace activist">peace activism</a>, he moved to <a href="/wiki/Manhattan" title="Manhattan">Manhattan</a> in 1971, where his criticism of the <a href="/wiki/Vietnam_War" title="Vietnam War">Vietnam War</a> resulted in a lengthy attempt by <a href="/wiki/Richard_Nixon" title="Richard Nixon">Richard Nixon</a>'s administration to deport him, while some of his songs were adopted as anthems by the <a href="/wiki/Anti-war_movement" title="Anti-war movement">anti-war movement</a> and the larger <a href="/wiki/Counterculture_of_the_1960s" title="Counterculture of the 1960s">counterculture</a>.</p>
<p>As of 2012, Lennon's solo album sales in the United States exceeded 14 million and, as writer, co-writer or performer, he is responsible for 25 number-one singles on the US <a href="/wiki/Billboard_Hot_100" title="Billboard Hot 100">Hot 100</a> chart. In 2002, a BBC poll on the <a href="/wiki/100_Greatest_Britons" title="100 Greatest Britons">100 Greatest Britons</a> voted him eighth and, in 2008, <i><a href="/wiki/Rolling_Stone" title="Rolling Stone">Rolling Stone</a></i> ranked him the fifth-greatest singer of all time. He was posthumously inducted into the <a href="/wiki/Songwriters_Hall_of_Fame" title="Songwriters Hall of Fame">Songwriters Hall of Fame</a> in 1987 and into the <a href="/wiki/Rock_and_Roll_Hall_of_Fame" title="Rock and Roll Hall of Fame">Rock and Roll Hall of Fame</a> in 1994.</p>
<p></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Biography">Biography</span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1940.E2.80.9357:_Early_years">1940–57: Early years</span></h3>
<p>Lennon was born in war-time England, on 9 October 1940 at Liverpool Maternity Hospital to <a href="/wiki/Julia_Lennon" title="Julia Lennon">Julia</a> (née Stanley) and <a href="/wiki/Alfred_Lennon" title="Alfred Lennon">Alfred Lennon</a>, a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Merchant_Navy" title="Merchant Navy">merchant seaman</a> of Irish descent, who was away at the time of his son's birth.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry2000b504_1-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry2000b504-1"><span>[</span>1<span>]</span></a></sup> His parents named him John Winston Lennon after his paternal grandfather, John "Jack" Lennon, and then-Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Winston_Churchill" title="Winston Churchill">Winston Churchill</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESpitz200524:_.22Julia_offered_the_name_in_honour_of.C2.A0..._Winston_Churchill.22_2-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESpitz200524:_.22Julia_offered_the_name_in_honour_of.C2.A0..._Winston_Churchill.22-2"><span>[</span>2<span>]</span></a></sup> His father was often away from home but sent regular pay cheques to 9 Newcastle Road, Liverpool, where Lennon lived with his mother,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESpitz200524:_.22The_entire_Stanley_clan_gathered_nightly_at_Newcastle_Road.22_3-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESpitz200524:_.22The_entire_Stanley_clan_gathered_nightly_at_Newcastle_Road.22-3"><span>[</span>3<span>]</span></a></sup> but the cheques stopped when he went <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/AWOL" title="AWOL">absent without leave</a> in February 1944.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELennon200554:_.22Until_then_he_had_sent_her_money_each_month_from_his_wages.2C_but_now_it_stopped.22_4-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELennon200554:_.22Until_then_he_had_sent_her_money_each_month_from_his_wages.2C_but_now_it_stopped.22-4"><span>[</span>4<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESpitz200526:_.22In_February_1944.C2.A0..._he_was_arrested_and_imprisoned._Freddie_subsequently_disappeared_for_six_months.22_5-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESpitz200526:_.22In_February_1944.C2.A0..._he_was_arrested_and_imprisoned._Freddie_subsequently_disappeared_for_six_months.22-5"><span>[</span>5<span>]</span></a></sup> When he eventually came home six months later, he offered to look after the family, but Julia—by then pregnant with another man's child—rejected the idea.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESpitz200527_6-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESpitz200527-6"><span>[</span>6<span>]</span></a></sup> After her sister, <a href="/wiki/Mimi_Smith" title="Mimi Smith">Mimi Smith</a>, twice complained to Liverpool's Social Services, Julia handed the care of Lennon over to her. In July 1946 Lennon's father visited Smith and took his son to Blackpool, secretly intending to emigrate to New Zealand with him.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELennon200556:_.22Alf_admitted_to_her_that_he_had_planned_to_take_John_to_live_in_New_Zealand.22_7-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELennon200556:_.22Alf_admitted_to_her_that_he_had_planned_to_take_John_to_live_in_New_Zealand.22-7"><span>[</span>7<span>]</span></a></sup> Julia followed them—with her partner at the time, 'Bobby' Dykins—and after a heated argument his father forced the five-year-old to choose between them. Lennon twice chose his father, but as his mother walked away, he began to cry and followed her.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESpitz200530:_.22Julia_went_out_of_the_door.C2.A0..._John_ran_after_her.22_8-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESpitz200530:_.22Julia_went_out_of_the_door.C2.A0..._John_ran_after_her.22-8"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup> It would be 20 years before he had contact with his father again.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESpitz2005497_9-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESpitz2005497-9"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Mendipsnationaltrust.JPG"><img alt="A grey two-story building, with numerous windows visible on both levels" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1704" data-file-width="2272" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Mendipsnationaltrust.JPG/220px-Mendipsnationaltrust.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Mendipsnationaltrust.JPG/330px-Mendipsnationaltrust.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Mendipsnationaltrust.JPG/440px-Mendipsnationaltrust.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Mendipsnationaltrust.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
251 Menlove Avenue, where Lennon lived for most of his childhood</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Throughout the rest of his childhood and adolescence he lived with his aunt and uncle, Mimi and <a href="/wiki/George_Toogood_Smith" title="George Toogood Smith">George Smith</a>, who had no children of their own, at <a href="/wiki/251_Menlove_Avenue" title="251 Menlove Avenue">Mendips, 251 Menlove Avenue</a>, <a href="/wiki/Woolton" title="Woolton">Woolton</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELennon200556:_.22Hard_to_see_why_Mimi_wanted_John.2C_as_she_had_always_said_she_didn.27t_want_children.22_10-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELennon200556:_.22Hard_to_see_why_Mimi_wanted_John.2C_as_she_had_always_said_she_didn.27t_want_children.22-10"><span>[</span>10<span>]</span></a></sup> His aunt purchased volumes of short stories for him, and his uncle, a dairyman at his family's farm, bought him a mouth organ and engaged him in solving <a class="extiw" href="//en.wiktionary.org/wiki/crossword" title="wiktionary:crossword">crossword</a> puzzles.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESpitz200532:_.22When_he_was_old_enough.2C_taught_John_how_to_solve_crossword_puzzles.22_11-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESpitz200532:_.22When_he_was_old_enough.2C_taught_John_how_to_solve_crossword_puzzles.22-11"><span>[</span>11<span>]</span></a></sup> Julia visited Mendips on a regular basis, and when John was 11 years old he often visited her at 1 Blomfield Road, Liverpool, where she played him <a href="/wiki/Elvis_Presley" title="Elvis Presley">Elvis Presley</a> records, taught him the banjo, and showed him how to play "<a href="/wiki/Ain%27t_That_a_Shame" title="Ain't That a Shame">Ain't That a Shame</a>" by <a href="/wiki/Fats_Domino" title="Fats Domino">Fats Domino</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESpitz200548:_.22To_get_them_started.2C_she_applied_the_triad_to_.27Ain.27t_That_a_Shame.27.22_12-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESpitz200548:_.22To_get_them_started.2C_she_applied_the_triad_to_.27Ain.27t_That_a_Shame.27.22-12"><span>[</span>12<span>]</span></a></sup> In September 1980, Lennon commented about his family and his rebellious nature:</p>
<blockquote class="templatequote">
<p>Part of me would like to be accepted by all facets of society and <i>not</i> be this loudmouthed lunatic poet/musician. But I cannot be what I am not ... I was the one who all the other boys' parents—including Paul's father—would say, 'Keep away from him'... The parents instinctively recognised I was a troublemaker, meaning I did not conform and I would influence their children, which I did. I did my best to disrupt every friend's home ... Partly out of envy that I didn't have this so-called home ... but I <i>did</i>... There were five women that were my family. Five <i>strong</i>, <i>intelligent</i>, <i>beautiful</i> women, five sisters. One happened to be my mother. [She] just couldn't deal with life. She was the youngest and she had a husband who ran away to sea and the war was on and she couldn't cope with me, and I ended up living with her elder sister. Now those women were fantastic ... And that was my first feminist education ... I would infiltrate the other boys minds. I could say, "Parents are not gods because I don't live with mine and, therefore, I know.'<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESheff1981134.E2.80.93136_13-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESheff1981134.E2.80.93136-13"><span>[</span>13<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
</blockquote>
<p>He regularly visited his cousin, Stanley Parkes, who lived in <a href="/wiki/Fleetwood" title="Fleetwood">Fleetwood</a>. Seven years Lennon's senior, Parkes took him on trips and to local cinemas.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESpitz200532:_.22Parkes_recalled.C2.A0..._Leila_and_John_to_the_cinema_as_often_as_three_times_a_day.22_14-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESpitz200532:_.22Parkes_recalled.C2.A0..._Leila_and_John_to_the_cinema_as_often_as_three_times_a_day.22-14"><span>[</span>14<span>]</span></a></sup> During the school holidays, Parkes often visited Lennon with Leila Harvey, another cousin, often travelling to Blackpool two or three times a week to watch shows. They would visit the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Blackpool_Tower_Circus" title="Blackpool Tower Circus">Blackpool Tower Circus</a> and see artists such as <a href="/wiki/Dickie_Valentine" title="Dickie Valentine">Dickie Valentine</a>, <a href="/wiki/Arthur_Askey" title="Arthur Askey">Arthur Askey</a>, <a href="/wiki/Max_Bygraves" title="Max Bygraves">Max Bygraves</a> and <a href="/wiki/Joe_Loss" title="Joe Loss">Joe Loss</a>, with Parkes recalling that Lennon particularly liked <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/George_Formby,_Jr." title="George Formby, Jr.">George Formby</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry2009_15-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry2009-15"><span>[</span>15<span>]</span></a></sup> After Parkes's family moved to Scotland, the three cousins often spent their school holidays together there. Parkes recalled, "John, cousin Leila and I were very close. From Edinburgh we would drive up to the family croft at <a href="/wiki/Durness" title="Durness">Durness</a>, which was from about the time John was nine years old until he was about 16."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry2000b702_16-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry2000b702-16"><span>[</span>16<span>]</span></a></sup> He was 14 years old when his uncle George died of a liver haemorrhage on 5 June 1955 (aged 52).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry2000b819_17-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry2000b819-17"><span>[</span>17<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Lennon was raised as an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Anglican" title="Anglican">Anglican</a> and attended <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dovedale_Primary_School" title="Dovedale Primary School">Dovedale Primary School</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry2000b411_18-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry2000b411-18"><span>[</span>18<span>]</span></a></sup> From September 1952 to 1957, after passing his <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Eleven-Plus" title="Eleven-Plus">Eleven-Plus</a> exam, he attended <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Quarry_Bank_High_School" title="Quarry Bank High School">Quarry Bank High School</a> in Liverpool, and was described by Harvey at the time as, "A happy-go-lucky, good-humoured, easy going, lively lad."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESpitz200532.E2.80.9333_19-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESpitz200532.E2.80.9333-19"><span>[</span>19<span>]</span></a></sup> He often drew comical cartoons which appeared in his own self-made school magazine called <i>The Daily Howl</i>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESpitz200540_20-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESpitz200540-20"><span>[</span>20<span>]</span></a></sup> but despite his artistic talent, his school reports were damning: "Certainly on the road to failure ... hopeless ... rather a clown in class ... wasting other pupils' time."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEClassReports2008_21-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEClassReports2008-21"><span>[</span>21<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>His mother bought him his first guitar in 1956, an inexpensive <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gallotone_Champion" title="Gallotone Champion">Gallotone Champion</a> acoustic for which she "lent" her son five pounds and ten shillings on the condition that the guitar be delivered to her own house, and not Mimi's, knowing well that her sister was not supportive of her son's musical aspirations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESpitz200545_22-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESpitz200545-22"><span>[</span>22<span>]</span></a></sup> As Mimi was sceptical of his claim that he would be famous one day, she hoped he would grow bored with music, often telling him, "The guitar's all very well, John, but you'll never make a living out of it".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENorman200889_23-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENorman200889-23"><span>[</span>23<span>]</span></a></sup> On 15 July 1958, when Lennon was 17 years old, his mother, walking home after visiting the Smiths' house, was struck by a car and killed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMiles199748_24-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMiles199748-24"><span>[</span>24<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Lennon failed all his <a href="/wiki/General_Certificate_of_Education" title="General Certificate of Education">GCE</a> O-level examinations, and was accepted into the <a href="/wiki/Liverpool_College_of_Art" title="Liverpool College of Art">Liverpool College of Art</a> only after his aunt and headmaster intervened.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESpitz2005100_25-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESpitz2005100-25"><span>[</span>25<span>]</span></a></sup> Once at the college, he started wearing <a href="/wiki/Teddy_Boy" title="Teddy Boy">Teddy Boy</a> clothes and acquired a reputation for disrupting classes and ridiculing teachers. As a result, he was excluded from the painting class, then the graphic arts course, and was threatened with expulsion for his behaviour, which included sitting on a nude model's lap during a <a href="/wiki/Figure_drawing" title="Figure drawing">life drawing</a> class.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry2000b553.E2.80.93555_26-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry2000b553.E2.80.93555-26"><span>[</span>26<span>]</span></a></sup> He failed an annual exam, despite help from fellow student and future wife <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cynthia_Powell" title="Cynthia Powell">Cynthia Powell</a>, and was "thrown out of the college before his final year."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELennon200550_27-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELennon200550-27"><span>[</span>27<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1957.E2.80.9370:_The_Quarrymen_to_the_Beatles">1957–70: The Quarrymen to the Beatles</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote">Further information: <a href="/wiki/The_Quarrymen" title="The Quarrymen">The Quarrymen</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lennon%E2%80%93McCartney" title="Lennon–McCartney">Lennon–McCartney</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brian_Epstein" title="Brian Epstein">Brian Epstein</a>, <a href="/wiki/The_Beatles" title="The Beatles">The Beatles</a>, <a href="/wiki/Beatlemania" title="Beatlemania">Beatlemania</a>, <a href="/wiki/British_Invasion" title="British Invasion">British Invasion</a> and <a href="/wiki/More_popular_than_Jesus" title="More popular than Jesus">More popular than Jesus</a></div>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="1957.E2.80.9366:_Formation.2C_commercial_break-out_and_touring_years">1957–66: Formation, commercial break-out and touring years</span></h4>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:The_Bealtes_with_Jimmie_Nicol_916-5099.jpg"><img alt="Monochrome image of The Beatles performing on a stage wearing dark suits." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="844" data-file-width="1280" height="145" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/The_Bealtes_with_Jimmie_Nicol_916-5099.jpg/220px-The_Bealtes_with_Jimmie_Nicol_916-5099.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/The_Bealtes_with_Jimmie_Nicol_916-5099.jpg/330px-The_Bealtes_with_Jimmie_Nicol_916-5099.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/The_Bealtes_with_Jimmie_Nicol_916-5099.jpg/440px-The_Bealtes_with_Jimmie_Nicol_916-5099.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:The_Bealtes_with_Jimmie_Nicol_916-5099.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Lennon (right) performing with <a href="/wiki/The_Beatles" title="The Beatles">the Beatles</a> in 1964 at the height of <a href="/wiki/Beatlemania" title="Beatlemania">Beatlemania</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>At age 15, Lennon formed the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Skiffle_group" title="Skiffle group">skiffle group</a>, the Quarrymen. Named after Quarry Bank High School, the group was established by him in September 1956.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry2000b738_28-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry2000b738-28"><span>[</span>28<span>]</span></a></sup> By the summer of 1957, the Quarrymen played a "spirited set of songs" made up of half skiffle and half <a href="/wiki/Rock_and_roll" title="Rock and roll">rock and roll</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESpitz200595_29-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESpitz200595-29"><span>[</span>29<span>]</span></a></sup> Lennon first met Paul McCartney at the Quarrymen's second performance, held in Woolton on 6 July at the St. Peter's Church garden fête, after which he asked McCartney to join the band.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESpitz200593.E2.80.9399_30-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESpitz200593.E2.80.9399-30"><span>[</span>30<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>McCartney says that Aunt Mimi "was very aware that John's friends were lower class", and would often patronise him when he arrived to visit Lennon.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMiles199744_31-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMiles199744-31"><span>[</span>31<span>]</span></a></sup> According to Paul's brother Mike, McCartney's father was also disapproving, declaring Lennon would get his son "into trouble",<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMiles199732_32-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMiles199732-32"><span>[</span>32<span>]</span></a></sup> although he later allowed the fledgling band to rehearse in the McCartneys' front room at <a href="/wiki/20_Forthlin_Road" title="20 Forthlin Road">20 Forthlin Road</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMiles199738.E2.80.9339_33-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMiles199738.E2.80.9339-33"><span>[</span>33<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELennon200547_34-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELennon200547-34"><span>[</span>34<span>]</span></a></sup> During this time, the 18-year-old Lennon wrote his first song, "<a href="/wiki/Hello_Little_Girl" title="Hello Little Girl">Hello Little Girl</a>", a UK top 10 hit for <a href="/wiki/The_Fourmost" title="The Fourmost">The Fourmost</a> nearly five years later.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry2000b337.E2.80.93338_35-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry2000b337.E2.80.93338-35"><span>[</span>35<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>McCartney suggested his friend <a href="/wiki/George_Harrison" title="George Harrison">George Harrison</a> as the lead guitarist.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMiles199747.2C_50_36-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMiles199747.2C_50-36"><span>[</span>36<span>]</span></a></sup> Lennon thought Harrison (then 14 years old) was too young. McCartney engineered an audition on the upper deck of a Liverpool bus, where Harrison played "<a href="/wiki/Raunchy_(instrumental)" title="Raunchy (instrumental)">Raunchy</a>" for Lennon and was asked to join.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMiles199747_37-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMiles199747-37"><span>[</span>37<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Stuart_Sutcliffe" title="Stuart Sutcliffe">Stuart Sutcliffe</a>, Lennon's friend from art school, later joined as bassist.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELennon200564_38-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELennon200564-38"><span>[</span>38<span>]</span></a></sup> Lennon, McCartney, Harrison and Sutcliffe became "The Beatles" in early 1960. In August that year, the Beatles engaged for a 48-night <a href="/wiki/The_Beatles_in_Hamburg" title="The Beatles in Hamburg">residency in Hamburg</a>, Germany, and desperately in need of a drummer, asked <a href="/wiki/Pete_Best" title="Pete Best">Pete Best</a> to join them.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMiles199757_39-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMiles199757-39"><span>[</span>39<span>]</span></a></sup> Lennon was now 19, and his aunt, horrified when he told her about the trip, pleaded with him to continue his art studies instead.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELennon200553_40-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELennon200553-40"><span>[</span>40<span>]</span></a></sup> After the first Hamburg residency, the band accepted another in April 1961, and a third in April 1962. Like the other band members, Lennon was introduced to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Preludin" title="Preludin">Preludin</a> while in Hamburg,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMiles199766.E2.80.9367_41-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMiles199766.E2.80.9367-41"><span>[</span>41<span>]</span></a></sup> and regularly took the drug, as well as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Amphetamines" title="Amphetamines">amphetamines</a>, as a stimulant during their long, overnight performances.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELennon200557_42-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELennon200557-42"><span>[</span>42<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Brian_Epstein" title="Brian Epstein">Brian Epstein</a>, the Beatles' manager from 1962, had no prior experience of artist management, but had a strong influence on their early dress code and attitude on stage.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEThe_Beatles200067_43-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEThe_Beatles200067-43"><span>[</span>43<span>]</span></a></sup> Lennon initially resisted his attempts to encourage the band to present a professional appearance, but eventually complied, saying, "I'll wear a bloody balloon if somebody's going to pay me".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFrankel2007_44-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFrankel2007-44"><span>[</span>44<span>]</span></a></sup> McCartney took over on bass after Sutcliffe decided to stay in Hamburg, and drummer <a href="/wiki/Ringo_Starr" title="Ringo Starr">Ringo Starr</a> replaced Best, completing the four-piece line-up that would endure until the group's break-up in 1970. The band's first single, "<a href="/wiki/Love_Me_Do" title="Love Me Do">Love Me Do</a>", was released in October 1962 and reached No. 17 on the British charts. They recorded their debut album, <i><a href="/wiki/Please_Please_Me" title="Please Please Me">Please Please Me</a></i>, in under 10 hours on 11 February 1963,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry2000b721_45-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry2000b721-45"><span>[</span>45<span>]</span></a></sup> a day when Lennon was suffering the effects of a cold,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELewisohn198824.E2.80.9326:_.22Twist_and_Shout.2C_which_had_to_be_recorded_last_because_John_Lennon_had_a_particularly_bad_cold.22_46-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELewisohn198824.E2.80.9326:_.22Twist_and_Shout.2C_which_had_to_be_recorded_last_because_John_Lennon_had_a_particularly_bad_cold.22-46"><span>[</span>46<span>]</span></a></sup> which is evident in the vocal on the last song to be recorded that day, "<a href="/wiki/Twist_and_Shout" title="Twist and Shout">Twist and Shout</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESpitz2005376:_.22He_had_been_struggling_all_day_to_reach_notes.2C_but_this_was_different.2C_this_hurt.22_47-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESpitz2005376:_.22He_had_been_struggling_all_day_to_reach_notes.2C_but_this_was_different.2C_this_hurt.22-47"><span>[</span>47<span>]</span></a></sup> The Lennon–McCartney songwriting partnership yielded eight of its fourteen tracks. With few exceptions—one being the album title itself—Lennon had yet to bring his love of wordplay to bear on his song lyrics, saying: "We were just writing songs ... pop songs with no more thought of them than that—to create a sound. And the words were almost irrelevant".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry2000b721_45-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry2000b721-45"><span>[</span>45<span>]</span></a></sup> In a 1987 interview, McCartney said that the other Beatles idolised John: "He was like our own little Elvis ... We all looked up to John. He was older and he was very much the leader; he was the quickest wit and the smartest".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDoggett201033_48-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDoggett201033-48"><span>[</span>48<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:John_Lennon_1964_001_cropped.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="672" data-file-width="380" height="301" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/John_Lennon_1964_001_cropped.png/170px-John_Lennon_1964_001_cropped.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/John_Lennon_1964_001_cropped.png/255px-John_Lennon_1964_001_cropped.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/John_Lennon_1964_001_cropped.png/340px-John_Lennon_1964_001_cropped.png 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:John_Lennon_1964_001_cropped.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Lennon performing with <a href="/wiki/The_Beatles" title="The Beatles">the Beatles</a> in 1964.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The Beatles achieved mainstream success in the UK during the beginning of 1963. Lennon was on tour when his first son, <a href="/wiki/Julian_Lennon" title="Julian Lennon">Julian</a>, was born in April. During their <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Royal_Variety_Show" title="Royal Variety Show">Royal Variety Show</a> performance, attended by the Queen Mother and other British royalty, Lennon poked fun at his audience: "For our next song, I'd like to ask for your help. For the people in the cheaper seats, clap your hands ... and the rest of you, if you'll just rattle your jewellery."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEShennan2007_49-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEShennan2007-49"><span>[</span>49<span>]</span></a></sup> After a year of <a href="/wiki/Beatlemania_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="Beatlemania in the United Kingdom">Beatlemania in the UK</a>, the group's historic February 1964 US debut appearance on <i><a href="/wiki/The_Ed_Sullivan_Show" title="The Ed Sullivan Show">The Ed Sullivan Show</a></i> marked their breakthrough to international stardom. A two-year period of constant touring, moviemaking, and songwriting followed, during which Lennon wrote two books, <i><a href="/wiki/In_His_Own_Write" title="In His Own Write">In His Own Write</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/A_Spaniard_in_the_Works" title="A Spaniard in the Works">A Spaniard in the Works</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEColeman1984a239.E2.80.93240_50-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEColeman1984a239.E2.80.93240-50"><span>[</span>50<span>]</span></a></sup> The Beatles received recognition from the British Establishment when they were appointed <a href="/wiki/Order_of_the_British_Empire" title="Order of the British Empire">Members of the Order of the British Empire</a> (MBE) in the <a href="/wiki/1965_Birthday_Honours" title="1965 Birthday Honours">1965 Queen's Birthday Honours</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELondon_Gazette19655487.E2.80.935489_51-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELondon_Gazette19655487.E2.80.935489-51"><span>[</span>51<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Lennon grew concerned that fans attending Beatles concerts were unable to hear the music above the screaming of fans, and that the band's musicianship was beginning to suffer as a result.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEColeman1984a288_52-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEColeman1984a288-52"><span>[</span>52<span>]</span></a></sup> Lennon's "<a href="/wiki/Help!_(song)" title="Help! (song)">Help!</a>" expressed his own feelings in 1965: "I <i>meant</i> it ... It was me singing 'help'".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGould2008268_53-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGould2008268-53"><span>[</span>53<span>]</span></a></sup> He had put on weight (he would later refer to this as his "Fat Elvis" period),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELawrence200562_54-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELawrence200562-54"><span>[</span>54<span>]</span></a></sup> and felt he was subconsciously seeking change.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEThe_Beatles2000171_55-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEThe_Beatles2000171-55"><span>[</span>55<span>]</span></a></sup> The following January he was unknowingly introduced to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/LSD" title="LSD">LSD</a> when a dentist, hosting a dinner party attended by Lennon, Harrison and their wives, spiked the guests' coffee with the drug.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry2000b570_56-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry2000b570-56"><span>[</span>56<span>]</span></a></sup> When they wanted to leave, their host revealed what they had taken, and strongly advised them not to leave the house because of the likely effects. Later, in an elevator at a nightclub, they all believed it was on fire: "We were all screaming ... hot and hysterical."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry2000b570_56-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry2000b570-56"><span>[</span>56<span>]</span></a></sup> <span id="BiggerThanJesus"></span> A few months later in March, during an interview with <i>Evening Standard</i> reporter <a href="/wiki/Maureen_Cleave" title="Maureen Cleave">Maureen Cleave</a>, Lennon remarked, "Christianity will go. It will vanish and shrink ... We're more popular than Jesus now—I don't know which will go first, rock and roll or Christianity."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECleave2007_57-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECleave2007-57"><span>[</span>57<span>]</span></a></sup> The comment went virtually unnoticed in England but caused <a href="/wiki/More_popular_than_Jesus" title="More popular than Jesus">great offence in the US</a> when quoted by a magazine there five months later. The furore that followed—burning of Beatles records, <a href="/wiki/Ku_Klux_Klan" title="Ku Klux Klan">Ku Klux Klan</a> activity and threats against Lennon—contributed to the band's decision to stop touring.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGould20085.E2.80.936.2C_249.2C_281.2C_347_58-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGould20085.E2.80.936.2C_249.2C_281.2C_347-58"><span>[</span>58<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="1967.E2.80.9370:_Studio_years.2C_break-up_and_solo_work">1967–70: Studio years, break-up and solo work</span></h4>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Beatles-our-world.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="189" data-file-width="277" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/3/30/Beatles-our-world.jpg/220px-Beatles-our-world.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/3/30/Beatles-our-world.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/3/30/Beatles-our-world.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Beatles-our-world.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Lennon (right) performing "<a href="/wiki/All_You_Need_Is_Love" title="All You Need Is Love">All You Need Is Love</a>" with <a href="/wiki/The_Beatles" title="The Beatles">The Beatles</a> in 1967 to 400 million viewers of <i><a href="/wiki/Our_World_(TV_special)" title="Our World (TV special)">Our World</a>.</i></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Deprived of the routine of live performances after their final commercial concert on 29 August 1966, Lennon felt lost and considered leaving the band.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBrown1983222_59-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBrown1983222-59"><span>[</span>59<span>]</span></a></sup> Since his involuntary introduction to LSD in January, he had made increasing use of the drug, and was almost constantly under its influence for much of the year.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGould2008319_60-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGould2008319-60"><span>[</span>60<span>]</span></a></sup> According to biographer Ian MacDonald, Lennon's continuous experience with LSD during the year brought him "close to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Egolessness" title="Egolessness">erasing his identity</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMacDonald2005281_61-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMacDonald2005281-61"><span>[</span>61<span>]</span></a></sup> 1967 saw the release of "<a href="/wiki/Strawberry_Fields_Forever" title="Strawberry Fields Forever">Strawberry Fields Forever</a>", hailed by <i>Time</i> magazine for its "astonishing inventiveness",<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETime1967_62-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTETime1967-62"><span>[</span>62<span>]</span></a></sup> and the group's landmark album <i><a href="/wiki/Sgt._Pepper%27s_Lonely_Hearts_Club_Band" title="Sgt. Pepper's Lonely Hearts Club Band">Sgt. Pepper's Lonely Hearts Club Band</a></i>, which revealed Lennon's lyrics contrasting strongly with the simple love songs of the Lennon–McCartney's early years.</p>
<p>In August, after having been introduced to the <a href="/wiki/Maharishi_Mahesh_Yogi" title="Maharishi Mahesh Yogi">Maharishi Mahesh Yogi</a>, the group attended a weekend of personal instruction at his <a href="/wiki/Transcendental_Meditation" title="Transcendental Meditation">Transcendental Meditation</a> seminar in Bangor, Wales,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBBC_News2007b_63-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBBC_News2007b-63"><span>[</span>63<span>]</span></a></sup> and were informed of Epstein's death during the seminar. "I knew we were in trouble then", Lennon said later. "I didn't have any misconceptions about our ability to do anything other than play music, and I was scared".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBrown1983276_64-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBrown1983276-64"><span>[</span>64<span>]</span></a></sup> They later travelled to Maharishi's <a href="/wiki/Ashram" title="Ashram">ashram</a> in India for further guidance, where they composed most of the songs for <i><a href="/wiki/The_Beatles_(album)" title="The Beatles (album)">The Beatles</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Abbey_Road" title="Abbey Road">Abbey Road</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMiles1997397_65-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMiles1997397-65"><span>[</span>65<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The anti-war, black comedy <i><a href="/wiki/How_I_Won_the_War" title="How I Won the War">How I Won the War</a></i>, featuring Lennon's only appearance in a non–Beatles full-length film, was shown in cinemas in October 1967.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHoppa2010_66-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHoppa2010-66"><span>[</span>66<span>]</span></a></sup> McCartney organised the group's first post-Epstein project,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMiles1997349-373_67-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMiles1997349-373-67"><span>[</span>67<span>]</span></a></sup> the self-written, -produced and -directed television film <i><a href="/wiki/Magical_Mystery_Tour_(film)" title="Magical Mystery Tour (film)">Magical Mystery Tour</a></i>, released in December that year. While the film itself proved to be their first critical flop, its <a href="/wiki/Magical_Mystery_Tour" title="Magical Mystery Tour">soundtrack release</a>, featuring Lennon's acclaimed, <a href="/wiki/Lewis_Carroll" title="Lewis Carroll">Lewis Carroll</a>-inspired "<a href="/wiki/I_Am_the_Walrus" title="I Am the Walrus">I Am the Walrus</a>", was a success.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELogan1967_68-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELogan1967-68"><span>[</span>68<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELewisohn1988131_69-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELewisohn1988131-69"><span>[</span>69<span>]</span></a></sup> With Epstein gone, the band members became increasingly involved in business activities, and in February 1968 they formed <a href="/wiki/Apple_Corps" title="Apple Corps">Apple Corps</a>, a multimedia corporation composed of <a href="/wiki/Apple_Records" title="Apple Records">Apple Records</a> and several other subsidiary companies. Lennon described the venture as an attempt to achieve, "artistic freedom within a business structure",<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry2000b31_70-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry2000b31-70"><span>[</span>70<span>]</span></a></sup> but his increased drug experimentation and growing preoccupation with <a href="/wiki/Yoko_Ono" title="Yoko Ono">Yoko Ono</a>, and McCartney's own marriage plans, left Apple in need of professional management. Lennon asked <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lord_Beeching" title="Lord Beeching">Lord Beeching</a> to take on the role, but he declined, advising Lennon to go back to making records. Lennon approached <a href="/wiki/Allen_Klein" title="Allen Klein">Allen Klein</a>, who had managed <a href="/wiki/The_Rolling_Stones" title="The Rolling Stones">The Rolling Stones</a> and other bands during the <a href="/wiki/British_Invasion" title="British Invasion">British Invasion</a>. Klein was appointed as Apple's chief executive by Lennon, Harrison and Starr,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETelegraphKlein2010_71-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTETelegraphKlein2010-71"><span>[</span>71<span>]</span></a></sup> but McCartney never signed the management contract.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMiles1997549:_.22Paul_never_did_sign_the_management_contract.22_72-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMiles1997549:_.22Paul_never_did_sign_the_management_contract.22-72"><span>[</span>72<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<table class="mbox-small-left" style="border:1px solid #aaa;background-color:#f9f9f9;float:left">
<tr>
<td class="mbox-image">
<div class="center">
<div class="floatnone"><img alt="" data-file-height="160" data-file-width="160" height="50" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Gnome-mime-audio-openclipart.svg/50px-Gnome-mime-audio-openclipart.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Gnome-mime-audio-openclipart.svg/75px-Gnome-mime-audio-openclipart.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Gnome-mime-audio-openclipart.svg/100px-Gnome-mime-audio-openclipart.svg.png 2x" width="50"/></div>

</td>

<div class="description" style="padding:2px 0 0 0">Sample of "<a href="/wiki/Give_Peace_a_Chance" title="Give Peace a Chance">Give Peace a Chance</a>", recorded in 1969 during Lennon and Ono's second <a href="/wiki/Bed-In" title="Bed-In">Bed-In for Peace</a>. As described by biographer Bill Harry, Lennon wanted to "write a peace anthem that would take over from the song '<a href="/wiki/We_Shall_Overcome" title="We Shall Overcome">We Shall Overcome</a>'—and he succeeded ... it became the main anti-<a href="/wiki/Vietnam_War" title="Vietnam War">Vietnam</a> protest song."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry2000b276.E2.80.93278_73-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry2000b276.E2.80.93278-73"><span>[</span>73<span>]</span></a></sup></div>
</div>
<hr/></td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td class="mbox-text" colspan="2" style="line-height:1.1em"><span style="font-size:smaller;"><i>Problems playing this file? See <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Media_help" title="Wikipedia:Media help">media help</a>.</i></span></td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>At the end of 1968, Lennon featured in the film <i><a href="/wiki/The_Rolling_Stones_Rock_and_Roll_Circus" title="The Rolling Stones Rock and Roll Circus">The Rolling Stones Rock and Roll Circus</a></i> (not released until 1996) in the role of a <a href="/wiki/The_Dirty_Mac" title="The Dirty Mac">Dirty Mac</a> band member. The <a href="/wiki/Supergroup_(music)" title="Supergroup (music)">supergroup</a>, composed of Lennon, <a href="/wiki/Eric_Clapton" title="Eric Clapton">Eric Clapton</a>, <a href="/wiki/Keith_Richards" title="Keith Richards">Keith Richards</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mitch_Mitchell" title="Mitch Mitchell">Mitch Mitchell</a>, also backed a vocal performance by Ono in the film.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry2000b774.E2.80.93775_74-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry2000b774.E2.80.93775-74"><span>[</span>74<span>]</span></a></sup> Lennon and Ono were married on 20 March 1969, and soon released a series of 14 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lithograph" title="Lithograph">lithographs</a> called "Bag One" depicting scenes from their honeymoon,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFawcett1976185_75-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFawcett1976185-75"><span>[</span>75<span>]</span></a></sup> eight of which were deemed indecent and most of which were banned and confiscated.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEColeman1984a279_76-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEColeman1984a279-76"><span>[</span>76<span>]</span></a></sup> Lennon's creative focus continued to move beyond the Beatles and between 1968 and 1969 he and Ono recorded three albums of experimental music together: <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Unfinished_Music_No.1:_Two_Virgins" title="Unfinished Music No.1: Two Virgins">Unfinished Music No.1: Two Virgins</a></i><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEColeman1984a48.E2.80.9349_77-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEColeman1984a48.E2.80.9349-77"><span>[</span>77<span>]</span></a></sup> (known more for its cover than for its music), <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Unfinished_Music_No.2:_Life_with_the_Lions" title="Unfinished Music No.2: Life with the Lions">Unfinished Music No.2: Life with the Lions</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Wedding_Album" title="Wedding Album">Wedding Album</a></i>. In 1969, they formed the <a href="/wiki/Plastic_Ono_Band" title="Plastic Ono Band">Plastic Ono Band</a>, releasing <i><a href="/wiki/Live_Peace_in_Toronto_1969" title="Live Peace in Toronto 1969">Live Peace in Toronto 1969</a></i>. Between 1969 and 1970, Lennon released the singles "Give Peace a Chance" (widely adopted as an anti-Vietnam-War anthem in 1969),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPerone200157.E2.80.9358_78-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPerone200157.E2.80.9358-78"><span>[</span>78<span>]</span></a></sup> "<a href="/wiki/Cold_Turkey" title="Cold Turkey">Cold Turkey</a>" (documenting his withdrawal symptoms after he became addicted to heroin<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry2000b160.E2.80.93161_79-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry2000b160.E2.80.93161-79"><span>[</span>79<span>]</span></a></sup>) and "<a href="/wiki/Instant_Karma!" title="Instant Karma!">Instant Karma!</a>". In protest at Britain's involvement in the <a href="/wiki/Nigerian_Civil_War" title="Nigerian Civil War">Nigerian Civil War</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMiles_and_Badman2003_80-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMiles_and_Badman2003-80"><span>[</span>80<span>]</span></a></sup> its support of America in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vietnam_war" title="Vietnam war">Vietnam war</a> and (perhaps jokingly) against "Cold Turkey" slipping down the charts,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81"><span>[</span>81<span>]</span></a></sup> Lennon returned his <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/MBE" title="MBE">MBE</a> medal to the Queen, though this had no effect on his MBE status, which could not be renounced.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry2000b615.E2.80.93617_82-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry2000b615.E2.80.93617-82"><span>[</span>82<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Lennon left the Beatles in September 1969,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEdmondson2010129.E2.80.93130_83-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEdmondson2010129.E2.80.93130-83"><span>[</span>83<span>]</span></a></sup> and agreed not to inform the media while the group renegotiated their recording contract, but he was outraged that McCartney publicised his own departure on releasing <a href="/wiki/McCartney_(album)" title="McCartney (album)">his debut solo album</a> in April 1970. Lennon's reaction was, "Jesus Christ! He gets all the credit for it!"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESpitz2005853.E2.80.9354_84-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESpitz2005853.E2.80.9354-84"><span>[</span>84<span>]</span></a></sup> He later wrote, "I started the band. I disbanded it. It's as simple as that."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELoker2009348_85-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELoker2009348-85"><span>[</span>85<span>]</span></a></sup> In later interviews with <i><a href="/wiki/Rolling_Stone" title="Rolling Stone">Rolling Stone</a></i> magazine, he revealed his bitterness towards McCartney, saying, "I was a fool not to do what Paul did, which was use it to sell a record."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWenner200032_86-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWenner200032-86"><span>[</span>86<span>]</span></a></sup> He spoke too of the hostility he perceived the other members had towards Ono, and of how he, Harrison, and Starr "got fed up with being sidemen for Paul ... After Brian Epstein died we collapsed. Paul took over and supposedly led us. But what is leading us when we went round in circles?"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWenner200024_87-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWenner200024-87"><span>[</span>87<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1970.E2.80.9380:_Solo_career">1970–80: Solo career</span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="1970.E2.80.9372:_Initial_solo_success_and_activism">1970–72: Initial solo success and activism</span></h4>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:John_Lennon_Imagine_1971.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1357" data-file-width="984" height="234" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/John_Lennon_Imagine_1971.jpg/170px-John_Lennon_Imagine_1971.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/John_Lennon_Imagine_1971.jpg/255px-John_Lennon_Imagine_1971.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/John_Lennon_Imagine_1971.jpg/340px-John_Lennon_Imagine_1971.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:John_Lennon_Imagine_1971.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Advertisement for "<a href="/wiki/Imagine_(John_Lennon_song)" title="Imagine (John Lennon song)">Imagine</a>" from <i>Billboard</i>, 18 September 1971.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 1970, Lennon and Ono went through <a href="/wiki/Primal_therapy#John_Lennon" title="Primal therapy">primal therapy</a> with Dr. <a href="/wiki/Arthur_Janov" title="Arthur Janov">Arthur Janov</a> in Los Angeles, California. Designed to release emotional pain from early childhood, the therapy entailed two half-days a week with Janov for four months; he had wanted to treat the couple for longer, but they felt no need to continue and returned to London.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry2000b408.E2.80.93410_88-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry2000b408.E2.80.93410-88"><span>[</span>88<span>]</span></a></sup> Lennon's emotional debut solo album, <i><a href="/wiki/John_Lennon/Plastic_Ono_Band" title="John Lennon/Plastic Ono Band">John Lennon/Plastic Ono Band</a></i> (1970), was received with high praise. Critic <a href="/wiki/Greil_Marcus" title="Greil Marcus">Greil Marcus</a> remarked, "John's singing in the last verse of 'God' may be the finest in all of rock."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBlaney200556_89-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBlaney200556-89"><span>[</span>89<span>]</span></a></sup> The album featured the songs "<a href="/wiki/Mother_(John_Lennon_song)" title="Mother (John Lennon song)">Mother</a>", in which Lennon confronted his feelings of childhood rejection,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry2000b640.E2.80.93641_90-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry2000b640.E2.80.93641-90"><span>[</span>90<span>]</span></a></sup> and the Dylanesque "<a href="/wiki/Working_Class_Hero" title="Working Class Hero">Working Class Hero</a>", a bitter attack against the bourgeois social system which, due to the lyric "you're still fucking peasants", fell foul of broadcasters.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERiley2002375_91-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERiley2002375-91"><span>[</span>91<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESchechter1997106_92-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESchechter1997106-92"><span>[</span>92<span>]</span></a></sup> The same year, <a href="/wiki/Tariq_Ali" title="Tariq Ali">Tariq Ali</a>'s revolutionary political views, expressed when he interviewed Lennon, inspired the singer to write "<a href="/wiki/Power_to_the_People_(song)" title="Power to the People (song)">Power to the People</a>". Lennon also became involved with Ali during a protest against <a href="/wiki/Oz_(magazine)" title="Oz (magazine)"><i>Oz</i> magazine's</a> prosecution for alleged obscenity. Lennon denounced the proceedings as "disgusting fascism", and he and Ono (as Elastic Oz Band) released the single "God Save Us/Do the Oz" and joined marches in support of the magazine.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWiener1990157_93-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWiener1990157-93"><span>[</span>93<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<table class="mbox-small" style="border:1px solid #aaa;background-color:#f9f9f9;">
<tr>
<td class="mbox-image">
<div class="center">
<div class="floatnone"><img alt="" data-file-height="160" data-file-width="160" height="50" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Gnome-mime-audio-openclipart.svg/50px-Gnome-mime-audio-openclipart.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Gnome-mime-audio-openclipart.svg/75px-Gnome-mime-audio-openclipart.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Gnome-mime-audio-openclipart.svg/100px-Gnome-mime-audio-openclipart.svg.png 2x" width="50"/></div>
</div>
</td>
<td class="mbox-text plainlist" style="line-height:1.1em">
<div class="haudio">

<div style="padding-right:4px">

<div class="description" style="padding:2px 0 0 0">Sample of "<a href="/wiki/Imagine_(John_Lennon_song)" title="Imagine (John Lennon song)">Imagine</a>", Lennon's "most famous post-Beatles track."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry2000b382_94-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry2000b382-94"><span>[</span>94<span>]</span></a></sup> Like "Give Peace a Chance", the song became an anti-war anthem, but its lyrics offended religious groups. Lennon's explanation was, "If you can imagine a world at peace, with no denominations of religion—not without religion, but without this 'my god is bigger than your god' thing—then it can be true."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry2000b382.E2.80.93383_95-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry2000b382.E2.80.93383-95"><span>[</span>95<span>]</span></a></sup></div>
</div>
<hr/></td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td class="mbox-text" colspan="2" style="line-height:1.1em"><span style="font-size:smaller;"><i>Problems playing this file? See <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Media_help" title="Wikipedia:Media help">media help</a>.</i></span></td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>With Lennon's next album, <i>Imagine</i> (1971), critical response was more guarded. <i>Rolling Stone</i> reported that "it contains a substantial portion of good music" but warned of the possibility that "his posturings will soon seem not merely dull but irrelevant".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGerson1971_96-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGerson1971-96"><span>[</span>96<span>]</span></a></sup> The album's title track would become an anthem for anti-war movements,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEVigilla2005_97-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEVigilla2005-97"><span>[</span>97<span>]</span></a></sup> while another, "<a href="/wiki/How_Do_You_Sleep%3F_(John_Lennon_song)" title="How Do You Sleep? (John Lennon song)">How Do You Sleep?</a>", was a musical attack on McCartney in response to lyrics from <i><a href="/wiki/Ram_(album)" title="Ram (album)">Ram</a></i> that Lennon felt, and McCartney later confirmed,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGoodman1984_98-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGoodman1984-98"><span>[</span>98<span>]</span></a></sup> were directed at him and Ono. However, Lennon softened his stance in the mid-1970s and said he had written "How Do You Sleep?" about himself.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry2000b354.E2.80.93356_99-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry2000b354.E2.80.93356-99"><span>[</span>99<span>]</span></a></sup> He said in 1980: "I used my resentment against Paul … to create a song … not a terrible vicious horrible vendetta […] I used my resentment and withdrawing from Paul and the Beatles, and the relationship with Paul, to write 'How Do You Sleep'. I don't really go 'round with those thoughts in my head all the time."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPeebles198144_100-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPeebles198144-100"><span>[</span>100<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Lennon and Ono moved to New York in August 1971, and in December released "<a href="/wiki/Happy_Xmas_(War_Is_Over)" title="Happy Xmas (War Is Over)">Happy Xmas (War Is Over)</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAllmusic2010f_101-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAllmusic2010f-101"><span>[</span>101<span>]</span></a></sup> The new year saw the <a href="/wiki/Presidency_of_Richard_Nixon" title="Presidency of Richard Nixon">Nixon administration</a> take what it called a "strategic counter-measure" against Lennon's anti-war and anti-Nixon propaganda, embarking on what would be a <a href="#Deportation_attempt">four-year attempt to deport him</a>. In 1972, Lennon and Ono attended a post-election wake held in the New York home of activist <a href="/wiki/Jerry_Rubin" title="Jerry Rubin">Jerry Rubin</a> after <a href="/wiki/George_McGovern" title="George McGovern">McGovern</a> lost to Nixon.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DeMain_102-0"><a href="#cite_note-DeMain-102"><span>[</span>102<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Glenn_103-0"><a href="#cite_note-Glenn-103"><span>[</span>103<span>]</span></a></sup> Embroiled in a continuing legal battle with the immigration authorities, Lennon was denied <a href="/wiki/Permanent_residence_(United_States)" title="Permanent residence (United States)">permanent residency in the US</a> (which wouldn't be resolved until 1976).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWiener1990204_104-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWiener1990204-104"><span>[</span>104<span>]</span></a></sup> Depressed, Lennon got intoxicated and had sex with a female guest, leaving Ono embarrassed. Her song "Death of Samantha" was inspired by the incident.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105"><a href="#cite_note-105"><span>[</span>105<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Recorded as a collaboration with Ono and with backing from the New York band <a href="/wiki/Elephant%27s_Memory" title="Elephant's Memory">Elephant's Memory</a>, <i><a href="/wiki/Some_Time_in_New_York_City" title="Some Time in New York City">Some Time in New York City</a></i> was released in 1972. Containing songs about women's rights, race relations, Britain's role in Northern Ireland and Lennon's problems obtaining a green card,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBBC_News2006a_106-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBBC_News2006a-106"><span>[</span>106<span>]</span></a></sup> the album was poorly received—unlistenable, according to one critic.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELandau1974_107-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELandau1974-107"><span>[</span>107<span>]</span></a></sup> "<a href="/wiki/Woman_Is_the_Nigger_of_the_World" title="Woman Is the Nigger of the World">Woman Is the Nigger of the World</a>", released as a US single from the album the same year, was televised on 11 May, on <i><a href="/wiki/The_Dick_Cavett_Show" title="The Dick Cavett Show">The Dick Cavett Show</a></i>. Many radio stations refused to broadcast the song because of the word "<a href="/wiki/Nigger" title="Nigger">nigger</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry2000b979.E2.80.93980_108-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry2000b979.E2.80.93980-108"><span>[</span>108<span>]</span></a></sup> Lennon and Ono gave two benefit concerts with Elephant's Memory and guests in New York in aid of patients at the <a href="/wiki/Willowbrook_State_School" title="Willowbrook State School">Willowbrook State School</a> mental facility.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDeming2008_109-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDeming2008-109"><span>[</span>109<span>]</span></a></sup> Staged at <a href="/wiki/Madison_Square_Garden" title="Madison Square Garden">Madison Square Garden</a> on 30 August 1972, they were his last full-length concert appearances.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEThe_Rock_and_Roll_Hall_of_Fame_and_Museum1994_110-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEThe_Rock_and_Roll_Hall_of_Fame_and_Museum1994-110"><span>[</span>110<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="1973.E2.80.9375:_.22Lost_weekend.22">1973–75: "Lost weekend"</span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:John_Lennon_last_television_interview_Tomorrow_show_1975.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="730" data-file-width="954" height="168" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/John_Lennon_last_television_interview_Tomorrow_show_1975.JPG/220px-John_Lennon_last_television_interview_Tomorrow_show_1975.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/John_Lennon_last_television_interview_Tomorrow_show_1975.JPG/330px-John_Lennon_last_television_interview_Tomorrow_show_1975.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/John_Lennon_last_television_interview_Tomorrow_show_1975.JPG/440px-John_Lennon_last_television_interview_Tomorrow_show_1975.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:John_Lennon_last_television_interview_Tomorrow_show_1975.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Publicity photo of John Lennon and host <a href="/wiki/Tom_Snyder" title="Tom Snyder">Tom Snyder</a> from the television program <i><a href="/wiki/Tomorrow_(TV_series)" title="Tomorrow (TV series)">Tomorrow</a></i>. Aired in 1975, this was the last television interview Lennon gave before his death in 1980.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>While Lennon was recording <i><a href="/wiki/Mind_Games_(John_Lennon_album)" title="Mind Games (John Lennon album)">Mind Games</a></i> (1973), he and Ono decided to separate. The ensuing 18-month period apart, which he later called his "<a href="/wiki/The_Lost_Weekend_(novel)" title="The Lost Weekend (novel)">lost weekend</a>",<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry2000b698.E2.80.93699_111-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry2000b698.E2.80.93699-111"><span>[</span>111<span>]</span></a></sup> was spent in Los Angeles and New York in the company of <a href="/wiki/May_Pang" title="May Pang">May Pang</a>. <i>Mind Games</i>, credited to the "Plastic U.F.Ono Band", was released in November 1973. Lennon also contributed "<a href="/wiki/I%27m_the_Greatest" title="I'm the Greatest">I'm the Greatest</a>" to Starr's album <i><a href="/wiki/Ringo_(album)" title="Ringo (album)">Ringo</a></i> (1973), released the same month (an alternate take, from the same 1973 <i>Ringo</i> sessions, with Lennon providing a guide vocal, appears on <i><a href="/wiki/John_Lennon_Anthology" title="John Lennon Anthology">John Lennon Anthology</a></i>).</p>
<p>In early 1974, Lennon was drinking heavily and his alcohol-fuelled antics with <a href="/wiki/Harry_Nilsson" title="Harry Nilsson">Harry Nilsson</a> made headlines. Two widely publicised incidents occurred at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Troubadour_(Los_Angeles)" title="The Troubadour (Los Angeles)">The Troubadour</a> club in March, the first when Lennon placed a <a href="/wiki/Sanitary_napkin" title="Sanitary napkin">menstruation "towel"</a> on his forehead and scuffled with a waitress, and the second, two weeks later, when Lennon and Nilsson were ejected from the same club after heckling the <a href="/wiki/Smothers_Brothers" title="Smothers Brothers">Smothers Brothers</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry2000b927.E2.80.93929_112-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry2000b927.E2.80.93929-112"><span>[</span>112<span>]</span></a></sup> Lennon decided to produce Nilsson's album <i><a href="/wiki/Pussy_Cats" title="Pussy Cats">Pussy Cats</a></i> and Pang rented a Los Angeles beach house for all the musicians<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry2000b735_113-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry2000b735-113"><span>[</span>113<span>]</span></a></sup> but after a month of further debauchery, with the recording sessions in chaos, Lennon moved to New York with Pang to finish work on the album. In April, Lennon had produced the <a href="/wiki/Mick_Jagger" title="Mick Jagger">Mick Jagger</a> song "Too Many Cooks (Spoil the Soup)" which was, for contractual reasons, to remain unreleased for more than 30 years. Pang supplied the recording for its eventual inclusion on <i><a href="/wiki/The_Very_Best_of_Mick_Jagger" title="The Very Best of Mick Jagger">The Very Best of Mick Jagger</a></i> (2007).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114"><a href="#cite_note-114"><span>[</span>114<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Settled back in New York, Lennon recorded the album <i><a href="/wiki/Walls_and_Bridges" title="Walls and Bridges">Walls and Bridges</a></i>. Released in October 1974, it yielded his only US <i>Hot 100</i> number-one non-Beatles single in his lifetime, "<a href="/wiki/Whatever_Gets_You_thru_the_Night" title="Whatever Gets You thru the Night">Whatever Gets You thru the Night</a>", featuring <a href="/wiki/Elton_John" title="Elton John">Elton John</a> on backing vocals and piano.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBadman20011974_115-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBadman20011974-115"><span>[</span>115<span>]</span></a></sup> (Although <i>Imagine</i> reached number-one on the US <i><a href="/wiki/Record_World" title="Record World">Record World</a></i> chart<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116"><a href="#cite_note-116"><span>[</span>116<span>]</span></a></sup> and in several other countries). A second single from the album, "<a href="/wiki/Number_9_Dream" title="Number 9 Dream">#9 Dream</a>", followed before the end of the year. Starr's <i><a href="/wiki/Goodnight_Vienna" title="Goodnight Vienna">Goodnight Vienna</a></i> (1974) again saw assistance from Lennon, who wrote the title track and played piano.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry2000b284_117-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry2000b284-117"><span>[</span>117<span>]</span></a></sup> On 28 November, Lennon made a surprise guest appearance at Elton John's Thanksgiving concert at <a href="/wiki/Madison_Square_Garden" title="Madison Square Garden">Madison Square Garden</a>, in fulfilment of his promise to join the singer in a live show if "Whatever Gets You thru the Night"—a song whose commercial potential Lennon had doubted—reached number one. Lennon performed the song along with "<a href="/wiki/Lucy_in_the_Sky_with_Diamonds" title="Lucy in the Sky with Diamonds">Lucy in the Sky with Diamonds</a>" and "<a href="/wiki/I_Saw_Her_Standing_There" title="I Saw Her Standing There">I Saw Her Standing There</a>", which he introduced as "a song by an old estranged fiancée of mine called Paul".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry2000b970_118-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry2000b970-118"><span>[</span>118<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Lennon co-wrote "<a href="/wiki/Fame_(David_Bowie_song)" title="Fame (David Bowie song)">Fame</a>", <a href="/wiki/David_Bowie" title="David Bowie">David Bowie</a>'s first US number one, and provided guitar and backing vocals for the January 1975 recording.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEThe_Rock_and_Roll_Hall_of_Fame_and_Museum1996_119-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEThe_Rock_and_Roll_Hall_of_Fame_and_Museum1996-119"><span>[</span>119<span>]</span></a></sup> The same month, Elton John topped the charts with his cover of "Lucy in the Sky with Diamonds", featuring Lennon on guitar and back-up vocals (Lennon is credited on the single under the moniker of "Dr. Winston O'Boogie"). He and Ono were reunited shortly afterwards. Lennon released <i><a href="/wiki/Rock_%27n%27_Roll_(John_Lennon_album)" title="Rock 'n' Roll (John Lennon album)">Rock 'n' Roll</a></i> (1975), an album of cover songs, in February. "<a href="/wiki/Stand_by_Me_(song)" title="Stand by Me (song)">Stand by Me</a>", taken from the album and a US and UK hit, became his last single for five years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry2000b240.2C_563_120-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry2000b240.2C_563-120"><span>[</span>120<span>]</span></a></sup> He made what would be his final stage appearance in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Associated_TeleVision" title="Associated TeleVision">ATV</a> special <i>A Salute to <a href="/wiki/Lew_Grade" title="Lew Grade">Lew Grade</a></i>, recorded on 18 April and televised in June.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry2000b758_121-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry2000b758-121"><span>[</span>121<span>]</span></a></sup> Playing acoustic guitar and backed by an eight-piece band, Lennon performed two songs from <i>Rock 'n' Roll</i> ("Stand by Me", which was not broadcast, and "Slippin' and Slidin'") followed by "Imagine".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry2000b758_121-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry2000b758-121"><span>[</span>121<span>]</span></a></sup> The band, known as Etc., wore masks behind their heads, a dig by Lennon who thought Grade was two-faced.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122"><a href="#cite_note-122"><span>[</span>122<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="1975.E2.80.9380:_Retirement_and_return">1975–80: Retirement and return</span></h4>
<p>With the birth of his second son <a href="/wiki/Sean_Lennon" title="Sean Lennon">Sean</a> on 9 October 1975, Lennon took on the role of househusband, beginning what would be a five-year hiatus from the music industry during which he gave all his attention to his family.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESheff1981_123-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESheff1981-123"><span>[</span>123<span>]</span></a></sup> Within the month, he fulfilled his contractual obligation to EMI/Capitol for one more album by releasing <i><a href="/wiki/Shaved_Fish" title="Shaved Fish">Shaved Fish</a></i>, a compilation album of previously recorded tracks.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESheff1981_123-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESheff1981-123"><span>[</span>123<span>]</span></a></sup> He devoted himself to Sean, rising at 6 am daily to plan and prepare his meals and to spend time with him.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry2000b553_124-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry2000b553-124"><span>[</span>124<span>]</span></a></sup> He wrote "Cookin' (In the Kitchen of Love)" for Starr's <i><a href="/wiki/Ringo%27s_Rotogravure" title="Ringo's Rotogravure">Ringo's Rotogravure</a></i> (1976), performing on the track in June in what would be his last recording session until 1980.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry2000b166_125-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry2000b166-125"><span>[</span>125<span>]</span></a></sup> He formally announced his break from music in Tokyo in 1977, saying, "we have basically decided, without any great decision, to be with our baby as much as we can until we feel we can take time off to indulge ourselves in creating things outside of the family."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBennahum199187_126-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBennahum199187-126"><span>[</span>126<span>]</span></a></sup> During his career break he created several series of drawings, and drafted a book containing a mix of autobiographical material and what he termed "mad stuff",<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry2000b814_127-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry2000b814-127"><span>[</span>127<span>]</span></a></sup> all of which would be published posthumously.</p>
<p>Lennon emerged from retirement in October 1980 with the single "<a href="/wiki/(Just_Like)_Starting_Over" title="(Just Like) Starting Over">(Just Like) Starting Over</a>", followed the next month by the album <i><a href="/wiki/Double_Fantasy" title="Double Fantasy">Double Fantasy</a></i>, which contained songs written during a journey to <a href="/wiki/Bermuda" title="Bermuda">Bermuda</a> on a 43-foot sailing boat the previous June,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBBC_News2006b_128-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBBC_News2006b-128"><span>[</span>128<span>]</span></a></sup> that reflected his fulfilment in his new-found stable family life.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESchinderSchwartz2007178_129-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESchinderSchwartz2007178-129"><span>[</span>129<span>]</span></a></sup> Sufficient additional material was recorded for a planned follow-up album <i><a href="/wiki/Milk_and_Honey_(album)" title="Milk and Honey (album)">Milk and Honey</a></i> (released posthumously in 1984).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGinell2009_130-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGinell2009-130"><span>[</span>130<span>]</span></a></sup> Released jointly by Lennon and Ono, <i>Double Fantasy</i> was not well received, drawing comments such as <i><a href="/wiki/Melody_Maker" title="Melody Maker">Melody Maker</a>'</i>s "indulgent sterility ... a godawful yawn".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBadman20011980_131-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBadman20011980-131"><span>[</span>131<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="8_December_1980:_Death">8 December 1980: Death</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Death_of_John_Lennon" title="Death of John Lennon">Death of John Lennon</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Strawberry_Fields_in_the_Central_Park_with_The_Dakota_behind.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1956" data-file-width="2708" height="159" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/Strawberry_Fields_in_the_Central_Park_with_The_Dakota_behind.jpg/220px-Strawberry_Fields_in_the_Central_Park_with_The_Dakota_behind.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/Strawberry_Fields_in_the_Central_Park_with_The_Dakota_behind.jpg/330px-Strawberry_Fields_in_the_Central_Park_with_The_Dakota_behind.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/Strawberry_Fields_in_the_Central_Park_with_The_Dakota_behind.jpg/440px-Strawberry_Fields_in_the_Central_Park_with_The_Dakota_behind.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Strawberry_Fields_in_the_Central_Park_with_The_Dakota_behind.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Strawberry Fields in Central Park with The Dakota in the background</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>At around 10:50 pm on 8 December 1980, as Lennon and Ono returned to their New York apartment in the <a href="/wiki/The_Dakota" title="The Dakota">Dakota</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mark_David_Chapman" title="Mark David Chapman">Mark David Chapman</a> shot Lennon in the back four times at the entrance to the building. Lennon was taken to the emergency room of nearby <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/St._Luke%27s-Roosevelt_Hospital_Center" title="St. Luke's-Roosevelt Hospital Center">Roosevelt Hospital</a> and was pronounced dead on arrival at 11:07 pm.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEIngham200682_132-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEIngham200682-132"><span>[</span>132<span>]</span></a></sup> Earlier that evening, Lennon had autographed a copy of <i>Double Fantasy</i> for Chapman.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry2000b145_133-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry2000b145-133"><span>[</span>133<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Ono issued a statement the next day, saying "There is no funeral for John", ending it with the words, "John loved and prayed for the human race. Please pray the same for him."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry2000b692_134-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry2000b692-134"><span>[</span>134<span>]</span></a></sup> His body was cremated at <a href="/wiki/Ferncliff_Cemetery" title="Ferncliff Cemetery">Ferncliff Cemetery</a> in <a href="/wiki/Hartsdale,_New_York" title="Hartsdale, New York">Hartsdale, New York</a>. Ono scattered his ashes in New York's <a href="/wiki/Central_Park" title="Central Park">Central Park</a>, where the <a href="/wiki/Strawberry_Fields_(memorial)" title="Strawberry Fields (memorial)">Strawberry Fields memorial</a> was later created.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry2000b510_135-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry2000b510-135"><span>[</span>135<span>]</span></a></sup> Chapman pleaded guilty to second-degree murder and was sentenced to 20 years to life.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-136"><a href="#cite_note-136"><span>[</span>136<span>]</span></a></sup> As of 2014<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=John_Lennon&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, he remains in prison, having been denied parole eight times.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-137"><a href="#cite_note-137"><span>[</span>137<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Personal_relationships">Personal relationships</span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cynthia_Lennon">Cynthia Lennon</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Cynthia_Lennon" title="Cynthia Lennon">Cynthia Lennon</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:John_and_Cynthia_on_car.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="435" data-file-width="325" height="228" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/6/61/John_and_Cynthia_on_car.JPG/170px-John_and_Cynthia_on_car.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/6/61/John_and_Cynthia_on_car.JPG/255px-John_and_Cynthia_on_car.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/6/61/John_and_Cynthia_on_car.JPG 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:John_and_Cynthia_on_car.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
John Lennon and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cynthia_Powell" title="Cynthia Powell">Cynthia Powell</a> in 1959</div>
</div>
</div>
