<p>Lennon and Cynthia Powell met in 1957 as fellow students at the <a href="/wiki/Liverpool_College_of_Art" title="Liverpool College of Art">Liverpool College of Art</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELennon200517.E2.80.9323_138-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELennon200517.E2.80.9323-138"><span>[</span>138<span>]</span></a></sup> Although being scared of Lennon's attitude and appearance, she heard that he was obsessed with French actress <a href="/wiki/Brigitte_Bardot" title="Brigitte Bardot">Brigitte Bardot</a>, so she dyed her hair blonde. Lennon asked her out, but when she said that she was engaged, he screamed out, "I didn't ask you to fuckin' marry me, did I?"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELennon200521_139-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELennon200521-139"><span>[</span>139<span>]</span></a></sup> She often accompanied him to Quarrymen gigs and travelled to Hamburg with McCartney's girlfriend at the time to visit him.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELennon200589.E2.80.9395_140-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELennon200589.E2.80.9395-140"><span>[</span>140<span>]</span></a></sup> Lennon, jealous by nature, eventually grew possessive and often terrified Powell with his anger and physical violence.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry2000b492.E2.80.93493_141-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry2000b492.E2.80.93493-141"><span>[</span>141<span>]</span></a></sup> Lennon later said that until he met Ono, he had never questioned his chauvinistic attitude to women. The Beatles song "<a href="/wiki/Getting_Better" title="Getting Better">Getting Better</a>", he said, told his own story, "I used to be cruel to my woman, and physically—any woman. I was a hitter. I couldn't express myself and I hit. I fought men and I hit women. That is why I am always on about peace".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESheff1981_123-2"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESheff1981-123"><span>[</span>123<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Recalling his reaction in July 1962 on learning that Cynthia was pregnant, Lennon said, "There's only one thing for it Cyn. We'll have to get married."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELennon200591_142-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELennon200591-142"><span>[</span>142<span>]</span></a></sup> The couple were married on 23 August at the <a href="/wiki/Mount_Pleasant,_Liverpool" title="Mount Pleasant, Liverpool">Mount Pleasant</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Register_Office" title="Register Office">Register Office</a> in Liverpool. His marriage began just as <a href="/wiki/Beatlemania_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="Beatlemania in the United Kingdom">Beatlemania</a> took hold across the UK. He performed on the evening of his wedding day, and would continue to do so almost daily from then on.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry2000b493.E2.80.93495_143-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry2000b493.E2.80.93495-143"><span>[</span>143<span>]</span></a></sup> Epstein, fearing that fans would be alienated by the idea of a married Beatle, asked the Lennons to keep their marriage secret. Julian was born on 8 April 1963; Lennon was on tour at the time and did not see his son until three days later.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELennon2005113_144-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELennon2005113-144"><span>[</span>144<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Cynthia attributes the start of the marriage breakdown to LSD, and as a result, she felt that he slowly lost interest in her.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry2000b496.E2.80.93497_145-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry2000b496.E2.80.93497-145"><span>[</span>145<span>]</span></a></sup> When the group travelled by train to <a href="/wiki/Bangor,_Gwynedd" title="Bangor, Gwynedd">Bangor</a>, Wales, in 1967, for the Maharishi Yogi's Transcendental Meditation seminar, a policeman did not recognise her and stopped her from boarding. She later recalled how the incident seemed to symbolise the ending of their marriage.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWarner_Brothers1988_146-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWarner_Brothers1988-146"><span>[</span>146<span>]</span></a></sup> After arriving home at <a href="/wiki/Kenwood,_St._George%27s_Hill" title="Kenwood, St. George's Hill">Kenwood</a>, and finding Lennon with Ono, Cynthia left the house to stay with friends. <a href="/wiki/Magic_Alex" title="Magic Alex">Alexis Mardas</a> later claimed to have slept with her that night, and a few weeks later he informed her that Lennon was seeking a divorce and custody of Julian on grounds of her adultery with him. After negotiations, Lennon capitulated and agreed to her divorcing him on the same grounds. The case was settled out of court, with Lennon giving her £100,000 and custody of Julian.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELennon2005305.E2.80.93306:_.22He_had_agreed_that_I_should_have_custody_of_Julian.22.2C_.22He_raised_his_offer_to_.C2.A3100.2C000.22_147-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELennon2005305.E2.80.93306:_.22He_had_agreed_that_I_should_have_custody_of_Julian.22.2C_.22He_raised_his_offer_to_.C2.A3100.2C000.22-147"><span>[</span>147<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Brian_Epstein">Brian Epstein</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:272px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Epstein_at_Hard_Days_Night.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="285" data-file-width="424" height="181" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a9/Epstein_at_Hard_Days_Night.jpg/270px-Epstein_at_Hard_Days_Night.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a9/Epstein_at_Hard_Days_Night.jpg/405px-Epstein_at_Hard_Days_Night.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/a/a9/Epstein_at_Hard_Days_Night.jpg 2x" width="270"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Epstein_at_Hard_Days_Night.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Starr, McCartney, Lennon, Harrison and Epstein at the preview of <i><a href="/wiki/A_Hard_Day%27s_Night_(film)" title="A Hard Day's Night (film)">A Hard Day's Night</a></i> in 1964</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="hatnote">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Brian_Epstein" title="Brian Epstein">Brian Epstein</a></div>
<p>The Beatles were performing at Liverpool's <a href="/wiki/The_Cavern_Club" title="The Cavern Club">Cavern Club</a> in 1962, when they were introduced to Epstein after a midday concert. Epstein was homosexual. According to biographer <a href="/wiki/Philip_Norman_(author)" title="Philip Norman (author)">Philip Norman</a>, one of his reasons for wanting to manage the group was that he was physically attracted to Lennon. Almost as soon as Julian was born, Lennon went on holiday to Spain with Epstein, leading to speculation about their relationship. Questioned about it later, Lennon said, "Well, it was almost a love affair, but not quite. It was never consummated. But it was a pretty intense relationship. It was my first experience with a homosexual that I was conscious was homosexual. We used to sit in a café in <a href="/wiki/Torremolinos" title="Torremolinos">Torremolinos</a> looking at all the boys and I'd say, 'Do you like that one? Do you like this one?' I was rather enjoying the experience, thinking like a writer all the time: I am experiencing this."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry2000a232_148-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry2000a232-148"><span>[</span>148<span>]</span></a></sup> Soon after their return from Spain, at McCartney's twenty-first birthday party in June 1963, Lennon physically attacked Cavern Club MC <a href="/wiki/Bob_Wooler" title="Bob Wooler">Bob Wooler</a> for saying "How was your honeymoon, John?" The MC, known for his wordplay and affectionate but cutting remarks, was making a joke,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry2000a1165.2C_1169_149-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry2000a1165.2C_1169-149"><span>[</span>149<span>]</span></a></sup> but ten months had passed since Lennon's marriage, and the honeymoon, deferred, was still two months in the future.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELennon200594.2C_119.E2.80.93120_150-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELennon200594.2C_119.E2.80.93120-150"><span>[</span>150<span>]</span></a></sup> To Lennon, who was intoxicated with alcohol at the time, the matter was simple: "He called me a <a href="/wiki/Queer" title="Queer">queer</a> so I battered his bloody ribs in".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry2000a1169_151-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry2000a1169-151"><span>[</span>151<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Lennon delighted in mocking Epstein for his homosexuality and for the fact that he was Jewish.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry2000b232_152-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry2000b232-152"><span>[</span>152<span>]</span></a></sup> When Epstein invited suggestions for the title of his autobiography, Lennon offered <i>Queer Jew</i>; on learning of the eventual title, <i><a href="/wiki/A_Cellarful_of_Noise" title="A Cellarful of Noise">A Cellarful of Noise</a></i>, he parodied, "More like <i>A Cellarful of Boys</i>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEColeman1992298.E2.80.93299_153-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEColeman1992298.E2.80.93299-153"><span>[</span>153<span>]</span></a></sup> He demanded of a visitor to Epstein's flat, "Have you come to blackmail him? If not, you're the only bugger in London who hasn't."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry2000b232_152-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry2000b232-152"><span>[</span>152<span>]</span></a></sup> During the recording of "<a href="/wiki/Baby,_You%27re_a_Rich_Man" title="Baby, You're a Rich Man">Baby, You're a Rich Man</a>", he sang altered choruses of "Baby, you're a rich fag Jew".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENorman2008503_154-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENorman2008503-154"><span>[</span>154<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMacDonald2005206_155-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMacDonald2005206-155"><span>[</span>155<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Julian_Lennon">Julian Lennon</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Julian_Lennon" title="Julian Lennon">Julian Lennon</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Julian_Lennon.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1348" data-file-width="1034" height="196" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Julian_Lennon.jpg/150px-Julian_Lennon.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Julian_Lennon.jpg/225px-Julian_Lennon.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Julian_Lennon.jpg/300px-Julian_Lennon.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Julian_Lennon.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Julian_Lennon" title="Julian Lennon">Julian Lennon</a> at the unveiling of the <a href="/wiki/John_Lennon_Peace_Monument" title="John Lennon Peace Monument">John Lennon Peace Monument</a> in Liverpool, October 2010</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Lennon's first son, Julian, was born as his commitments with the Beatles intensified <a href="/wiki/Beatlemania_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="Beatlemania in the United Kingdom">at the height of Beatlemania</a> during his marriage to Cynthia. Lennon was touring with the Beatles when Julian was born on 8 April 1963. Julian's birth, like his mother Cynthia's marriage to Lennon, was kept secret because Epstein was convinced public knowledge of such things would threaten the Beatles' commercial success. Julian recalls how some four years later, as a small child in <a href="/wiki/Weybridge" title="Weybridge">Weybridge</a>, "I was trundled home from school and came walking up with one of my watercolour paintings. It was just a bunch of stars and this blonde girl I knew at school. And Dad said, 'What's this?' I said, 'It's Lucy in the sky with diamonds.'"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry2000b517_156-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry2000b517-156"><span>[</span>156<span>]</span></a></sup> Lennon used it as the title of a <a href="/wiki/Lucy_in_the_Sky_with_Diamonds" title="Lucy in the Sky with Diamonds">Beatles song</a>, and though it was later reported to have been derived from the initials <a href="/wiki/Lysergic_acid_diethylamide" title="Lysergic acid diethylamide">LSD</a>, Lennon insisted, "It's not an acid song."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry2000b574_157-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry2000b574-157"><span>[</span>157<span>]</span></a></sup> McCartney corroborated Lennon's explanation that Julian innocently came up with the name.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry2000b574_157-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry2000b574-157"><span>[</span>157<span>]</span></a></sup> Lennon was distant from Julian, who felt closer to McCartney than to his father. During a car journey to visit Cynthia and Julian during Lennon's divorce, McCartney composed a song, "Hey Jules", to comfort him. It would evolve into the Beatles song "<a href="/wiki/Hey_Jude" title="Hey Jude">Hey Jude</a>". Lennon later said, "That's his best song. It started off as a song about my son Julian ... he turned it into 'Hey Jude'. I always thought it was about me and Yoko but he said it wasn't."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry2000b341_158-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry2000b341-158"><span>[</span>158<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Lennon's relationship with Julian was already strained, and after Lennon and Ono's 1971 move to New York, Julian would not see his father again until 1973.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPang2008back_cover_159-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPang2008back_cover-159"><span>[</span>159<span>]</span></a></sup> With Pang's encouragement, it was arranged for him (and his mother) to visit Lennon in Los Angeles, where they went to <a href="/wiki/Disneyland" title="Disneyland">Disneyland</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELennon2005252.E2.80.93255_160-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELennon2005252.E2.80.93255-160"><span>[</span>160<span>]</span></a></sup> Julian started to see his father regularly, and Lennon gave him a drumming part on a <i><a href="/wiki/Walls_and_Bridges" title="Walls and Bridges">Walls and Bridges</a></i> track.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELennon2005258_161-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELennon2005258-161"><span>[</span>161<span>]</span></a></sup> He bought Julian a <a href="/wiki/Gibson_Les_Paul" title="Gibson Les Paul">Gibson Les Paul</a> guitar and other instruments, and encouraged his interest in music by demonstrating guitar chord techniques.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELennon2005258_161-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELennon2005258-161"><span>[</span>161<span>]</span></a></sup> Julian recalls that he and his father "got on a great deal better" during the time he spent in New York: "We had a lot of fun, laughed a lot and had a great time in general."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETimes_Online2009_162-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTETimes_Online2009-162"><span>[</span>162<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In a <i>Playboy</i> interview with David Sheff shortly before his death, Lennon said, "Sean was a planned child, and therein lies the difference. I don't love Julian any less as a child. He's still my son, whether he came from a bottle of whiskey or because they didn't have pills in those days. He's here, he belongs to me, and he always will." He said he was trying to re-establish a connection with the then 17-year-old, and confidently predicted, "Julian and I will have a relationship in the future."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESheff1981_123-3"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESheff1981-123"><span>[</span>123<span>]</span></a></sup> After his death it was revealed that he had left Julian very little in his will.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBadman2003393_163-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBadman2003393-163"><span>[</span>163<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Yoko_Ono">Yoko Ono</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Yoko_Ono" title="Yoko Ono">Yoko Ono</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Lennons_by_Jack_Mitchell.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="507" data-file-width="600" height="186" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/Lennons_by_Jack_Mitchell.jpg/220px-Lennons_by_Jack_Mitchell.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/Lennons_by_Jack_Mitchell.jpg/330px-Lennons_by_Jack_Mitchell.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/Lennons_by_Jack_Mitchell.jpg/440px-Lennons_by_Jack_Mitchell.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Lennons_by_Jack_Mitchell.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Lennon and <a href="/wiki/Yoko_Ono" title="Yoko Ono">Yoko Ono</a> in 1980</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Two versions exist of how Lennon met Ono. According to the first, told by the Lennons, on 9 November 1966 Lennon went to the <a href="/wiki/Indica_Gallery" title="Indica Gallery">Indica Gallery</a> in London, where Ono was preparing her conceptual art exhibit, and they were introduced by gallery owner <a href="/wiki/John_Dunbar_(artist)" title="John Dunbar (artist)">John Dunbar</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry2000b682_164-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry2000b682-164"><span>[</span>164<span>]</span></a></sup> Lennon was intrigued by Ono's "Hammer A Nail": patrons hammered a nail into a wooden board, creating the art piece. Although the exhibition had not yet begun, Lennon wanted to hammer a nail into the clean board, but Ono stopped him. Dunbar asked her, "Don't you know who this is? He's a millionaire! He might buy it." Ono had supposedly not heard of the Beatles, but relented on condition that Lennon pay her five <a class="extiw" href="//en.wiktionary.org/wiki/shilling" title="wiktionary:shilling">shillings</a>, to which Lennon replied, "I'll give you an imaginary five shillings and hammer an imaginary nail in."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESheff1981_123-4"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESheff1981-123"><span>[</span>123<span>]</span></a></sup> The second version, told by McCartney, is that in late 1965, Ono was in London compiling original musical scores for a book <a href="/wiki/John_Cage" title="John Cage">John Cage</a> was working on, <i><a href="/wiki/Notations" title="Notations">Notations</a></i>, but McCartney declined to give her any of his own manuscripts for the book, suggesting that Lennon might oblige. When asked, Lennon gave Ono the original handwritten lyrics to "<a href="/wiki/The_Word_(song)" title="The Word (song)">The Word</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMiles1997272_165-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMiles1997272-165"><span>[</span>165<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Ono began telephoning and calling at Lennon's home, and when his wife asked for an explanation, he explained that Ono was only trying to obtain money for her "avant-garde bullshit".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry2000b683_166-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry2000b683-166"><span>[</span>166<span>]</span></a></sup> In May 1968, while his wife was on holiday in Greece, Lennon invited Ono to visit. They spent the night recording what would become the <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Two_Virgins" title="Two Virgins">Two Virgins</a></i> album, after which, he said, they "made love at dawn."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-167"><a href="#cite_note-167"><span>[</span>167<span>]</span></a></sup> When Lennon's wife returned home she found Ono wearing her bathrobe and drinking tea with Lennon who simply said, "Oh, hi."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELennon1978183_168-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELennon1978183-168"><span>[</span>168<span>]</span></a></sup> Ono became pregnant in 1968 and miscarried a male child they named John Ono Lennon II on 21 November 1968,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry2000b510_135-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry2000b510-135"><span>[</span>135<span>]</span></a></sup> a few weeks after Lennon's divorce from Cynthia was granted.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESpitz2005800_169-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESpitz2005800-169"><span>[</span>169<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>During Lennon's last two years in the Beatles, he and Ono began public protests against the <a href="/wiki/Vietnam_War" title="Vietnam War">Vietnam War</a>. They were married in <a href="/wiki/Gibraltar" title="Gibraltar">Gibraltar</a> on 20 March 1969,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEColeman1992705_170-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEColeman1992705-170"><span>[</span>170<span>]</span></a></sup> and spent their honeymoon at the <a href="/wiki/Hilton_Amsterdam" title="Hilton Amsterdam">Hilton Amsterdam</a> campaigning with a week-long <a href="/wiki/Bed-In" title="Bed-In">Bed-In for Peace</a>. They planned another Bed-In in the United States, but were denied entry,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKruse200916_171-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKruse200916-171"><span>[</span>171<span>]</span></a></sup> so held one instead at the <a href="/wiki/Queen_Elizabeth_Hotel" title="Queen Elizabeth Hotel">Queen Elizabeth Hotel</a> in Montreal, where they recorded "<a href="/wiki/Give_Peace_a_Chance" title="Give Peace a Chance">Give Peace a Chance</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry2000b276_172-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry2000b276-172"><span>[</span>172<span>]</span></a></sup> They often combined advocacy with performance art, as in their "<a href="/wiki/Bagism" title="Bagism">Bagism</a>", first introduced during a Vienna press conference. Lennon detailed this period in the Beatles song "<a href="/wiki/The_Ballad_of_John_and_Yoko" title="The Ballad of John and Yoko">The Ballad of John and Yoko</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEColeman1992550_173-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEColeman1992550-173"><span>[</span>173<span>]</span></a></sup> Lennon changed his name by <a href="/wiki/Deed_poll" title="Deed poll">deed poll</a> on 22 April 1969, adding "Ono" as a middle name. The brief ceremony took place on the roof of the <a href="/wiki/Apple_Corps" title="Apple Corps">Apple Corps</a> building, made famous three months earlier by the Beatles' <i><a href="/wiki/Let_It_Be" title="Let It Be">Let It Be</a></i> <a href="/wiki/The_Beatles%27_rooftop_concert" title="The Beatles' rooftop concert">rooftop concert</a>. Although he used the name John Ono Lennon thereafter, official documents referred to him as John Winston Ono Lennon, since he was not permitted to revoke a name given at birth.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEColeman1984b64_174-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEColeman1984b64-174"><span>[</span>174<span>]</span></a></sup> The couple settled at <a href="/wiki/Tittenhurst_Park" title="Tittenhurst Park">Tittenhurst Park</a> at <a href="/wiki/Sunninghill,_Berkshire" title="Sunninghill, Berkshire">Sunninghill</a> in <a href="/wiki/Berkshire" title="Berkshire">Berkshire</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENorman2008615_et_seq_175-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENorman2008615_et_seq-175"><span>[</span>175<span>]</span></a></sup> After Ono was injured in a car accident, Lennon arranged for a king-sized bed to be brought to the recording studio as he worked on the Beatles' last album, <i><a href="/wiki/Abbey_Road" title="Abbey Road">Abbey Road</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEmerickMassey2006279.E2.80.93280_176-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEmerickMassey2006279.E2.80.93280-176"><span>[</span>176<span>]</span></a></sup> To escape the acrimony of the band's break-up, Ono suggested they move permanently to New York, which they did on 31 August 1971.</p>
<p>They first lived in <a href="/wiki/The_St._Regis_Hotel" title="The St. Regis Hotel">The St. Regis Hotel</a> on 5th Avenue, East <a href="/wiki/55th_Street_(Manhattan)" title="55th Street (Manhattan)">55th Street</a>, then moved to a street-level flat at 105 <a href="/wiki/Bank_Street_(Manhattan)" title="Bank Street (Manhattan)">Bank Street</a>, <a href="/wiki/Greenwich_Village" title="Greenwich Village">Greenwich Village</a>, on 16 October 1971. After a robbery, they relocated to the more secure <a href="/wiki/The_Dakota" title="The Dakota">Dakota</a> at 1 West <a href="/wiki/72nd_Street_(Manhattan)" title="72nd Street (Manhattan)">72nd Street</a>, in May 1973.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-177"><a href="#cite_note-177"><span>[</span>177<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="May_Pang">May Pang</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote">Further information: <a href="/wiki/May_Pang" title="May Pang">May Pang</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:132px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:May_Pang_2002.jpg"><img alt="Profile picture of a bespectacled Asian woman in her early fifties. She has long red hair, and shows a toothy smile." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="504" data-file-width="367" height="179" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/May_Pang_2002.jpg/130px-May_Pang_2002.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/May_Pang_2002.jpg/195px-May_Pang_2002.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/May_Pang_2002.jpg/260px-May_Pang_2002.jpg 2x" width="130"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:May_Pang_2002.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/May_Pang" title="May Pang">May Pang</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>ABKCO Industries, formed in 1968 by <a href="/wiki/Allen_Klein" title="Allen Klein">Allen Klein</a> as an umbrella company to <a href="/wiki/ABKCO_Records" title="ABKCO Records">ABKCO Records</a>, recruited May Pang as a receptionist in 1969. Through involvement in a project with ABKCO, Lennon and Ono met her the following year. She became their personal assistant. After she had been working with the couple for three years, Ono confided that she and Lennon were becoming estranged from one another. She went on to suggest that Pang should begin a physical relationship with Lennon, telling her, "He likes you a lot." Pang, 22, astounded by Ono's proposition, eventually agreed to become Lennon's companion. The pair soon moved to California, beginning an 18-month period he later called his "<a href="/wiki/May_Pang#.22Lost_Weekend.22" title="May Pang">lost weekend</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry2000b698.E2.80.93699_111-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry2000b698.E2.80.93699-111"><span>[</span>111<span>]</span></a></sup> In Los Angeles, Pang encouraged Lennon to develop regular contact with Julian, whom he had not seen for two years. He also rekindled friendships with Starr, McCartney, Beatles roadie <a href="/wiki/Mal_Evans" title="Mal Evans">Mal Evans</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Harry_Nilsson" title="Harry Nilsson">Harry Nilsson</a>. Whilst drinking with Nilsson, after misunderstanding something Pang said, Lennon attempted to strangle her, relenting only when physically restrained by Nilsson.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry2000b700_178-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry2000b700-178"><span>[</span>178<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>On moving to New York, they prepared a spare room in their newly rented apartment for Julian to visit.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry2000b700_178-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry2000b700-178"><span>[</span>178<span>]</span></a></sup> Lennon, hitherto inhibited by Ono in this regard, began to reestablish contact with other relatives and friends. By December he and Pang were considering a house purchase, and he was refusing to accept Ono's telephone calls. In January 1975, he agreed to meet Ono—who said she had found a cure for smoking. But after the meeting he failed to return home or call Pang. When Pang telephoned the next day, Ono told her Lennon was unavailable, being exhausted after a hypnotherapy session. Two days later, Lennon reappeared at a joint dental appointment, stupefied and confused to such an extent that Pang believed he had been brainwashed. He told her his separation from Ono was now over, though Ono would allow him to continue seeing her as his <a href="/wiki/Mistress_(lover)" title="Mistress (lover)">mistress</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry2000b700.E2.80.93701_179-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry2000b700.E2.80.93701-179"><span>[</span>179<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sean_Lennon">Sean Lennon</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Sean_Lennon" title="Sean Lennon">Sean Lennon</a></div>
<p>When Lennon and Ono were reunited, she became pregnant, but having previously suffered three <a href="/wiki/Miscarriage" title="Miscarriage">miscarriages</a> in her attempt to have a child with Lennon, she said she wanted an abortion. She agreed to allow the pregnancy to continue on condition that Lennon adopt the role of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Househusband" title="Househusband">househusband</a>; this he agreed to do.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry2000b535.2C_690_180-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry2000b535.2C_690-180"><span>[</span>180<span>]</span></a></sup> Sean was born on 9 October 1975, Lennon's 35th birthday, delivered by <a href="/wiki/Caesarean_section" title="Caesarean section">Caesarean section</a>. Lennon's subsequent career break would span five years. He had a photographer take pictures of Sean every day of his first year, and created numerous drawings for him, posthumously published as <i>Real Love: The Drawings for Sean</i>. Lennon later proudly declared, "He didn't come out of my belly but, by God, I made his bones, because I've attended to every meal, and to how he sleeps, and to the fact that he swims like a fish."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry2000b535_181-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry2000b535-181"><span>[</span>181<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Former_Beatles">Former Beatles</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Collaborations_between_ex-Beatles" title="Collaborations between ex-Beatles">Collaborations between ex-Beatles</a>, <a href="/wiki/Paul_McCartney" title="Paul McCartney">Paul McCartney</a>, <a href="/wiki/George_Harrison" title="George Harrison">George Harrison</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ringo_Starr" title="Ringo Starr">Ringo Starr</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:The_Beatles_in_America.JPG"><img alt="Black-and-white picture of four young men outdoors in front of a staircase, surrounded by a large assembled crowd. All four are waving to the crowd." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2526" data-file-width="3578" height="155" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/The_Beatles_in_America.JPG/220px-The_Beatles_in_America.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/The_Beatles_in_America.JPG/330px-The_Beatles_in_America.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/The_Beatles_in_America.JPG/440px-The_Beatles_in_America.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:The_Beatles_in_America.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Lennon (left) and the rest of the Beatles <a href="/wiki/The_Beatles#.22British_Invasion.22" title="The Beatles">arriving in the US in 1964</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Although his friendship with Starr remained consistently friendly during the years following the Beatles' break-up in 1970, Lennon's relationships with McCartney and Harrison varied. He was close to Harrison initially, but the two drifted apart after Lennon moved to America. When Harrison was in New York for his December 1974 <i><a href="/wiki/Dark_Horse_(George_Harrison_album)" title="Dark Horse (George Harrison album)">Dark Horse</a></i> tour, Lennon agreed to join him on stage, but failed to appear after an argument over Lennon's refusal to sign an agreement that would finally dissolve the Beatles' legal partnership. (Lennon eventually signed the papers while holidaying in Florida with Pang and Julian.)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry2000b195_182-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry2000b195-182"><span>[</span>182<span>]</span></a></sup> Harrison incensed Lennon in 1980, when he published an autobiography that made little mention of him. Lennon told <i><a href="/wiki/Playboy" title="Playboy">Playboy</a></i>, "I was hurt by it. By glaring omission ... my influence on his life is absolutely zilch ... he remembers every two-bit sax player or guitarist he met in subsequent years. I'm not in the book."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry2000b327_183-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry2000b327-183"><span>[</span>183<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Lennon's most intense feelings were reserved for McCartney. In addition to attacking him through the lyrics of "<a href="/wiki/How_Do_You_Sleep%3F_(John_Lennon_song)" title="How Do You Sleep? (John Lennon song)">How Do You Sleep?</a>", Lennon argued with him through the press for three years after the group split. The two later began to reestablish something of the close friendship they had once known, and in 1974, they even played music together again before eventually growing apart once more. Lennon said that during McCartney's final visit, in April 1976, they watched the episode of <i><a href="/wiki/Saturday_Night_Live" title="Saturday Night Live">Saturday Night Live</a></i> in which <a href="/wiki/Lorne_Michaels" title="Lorne Michaels">Lorne Michaels</a> made a $3,000 cash offer to get the Beatles to reunite on the show.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry2000b934.E2.80.93935_184-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry2000b934.E2.80.93935-184"><span>[</span>184<span>]</span></a></sup> The pair considered going to the studio to make a joke appearance, attempting to claim their share of the money, but were too tired.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESheff1981_123-5"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESheff1981-123"><span>[</span>123<span>]</span></a></sup> Lennon summarised his feelings towards McCartney in an interview three days before his death: "Throughout my career, I've selected to work with ... only two people: Paul McCartney and Yoko Ono ... That ain't bad picking."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECohn2010.E2.80.93201195_185-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECohn2010.E2.80.93201195-185"><span>[</span>185<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Along with his estrangement from McCartney, Lennon always felt a musical competitiveness with him and kept an ear on his music. During his five-year career break he was content to sit back so long as McCartney was producing what Lennon saw as mediocre material.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESeaman1991122_186-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESeaman1991122-186"><span>[</span>186<span>]</span></a></sup> When McCartney released "<a href="/wiki/Coming_Up_(song)" title="Coming Up (song)">Coming Up</a>", in 1980, the year Lennon returned to the studio and the last year of his life, he took notice. "It's driving me crackers!" he jokingly complained, because he could not get the tune out of his head.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESeaman1991122_186-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESeaman1991122-186"><span>[</span>186<span>]</span></a></sup> Asked the same year whether the group were dreaded enemies or the best of friends, he replied that they were neither, and that he had not seen any of them in a long time. But he also said, "I still love those guys. The Beatles are over, but John, Paul, George and Ringo go on."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESheff1981_123-6"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESheff1981-123"><span>[</span>123<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Political_activism">Political activism</span></h2>
<div class="hatnote">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Bed-In" title="Bed-In">Bed-In</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bagism" title="Bagism">Bagism</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Jlbedin3.JPG"><img alt='Lennon and Ono sit in front of flowers and placards bearing the word "peace." Lennon is only partly visible, and he holds an acoustic guitar. Ono wears a white dress, and there is a hanging microphone in front of her. In the foreground of the image are three men, one of them a guitarist facing away, and a woman.' class="thumbimage" data-file-height="374" data-file-width="600" height="137" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/Jlbedin3.JPG/220px-Jlbedin3.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/Jlbedin3.JPG/330px-Jlbedin3.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/Jlbedin3.JPG/440px-Jlbedin3.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Jlbedin3.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Recording "Give Peace a Chance" during the <a href="/wiki/Bed-In" title="Bed-In">Bed-In for Peace</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Queen_Elizabeth_Hotel" title="Queen Elizabeth Hotel">Queen Elizabeth Hotel</a>, Montreal</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Lennon and Ono used their honeymoon as what they termed a "<a href="/wiki/Bed-In" title="Bed-In">Bed-In for Peace</a>" at the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Amsterdam_Hilton_Hotel" title="Amsterdam Hilton Hotel">Amsterdam Hilton Hotel</a>; the March 1969 event attracted worldwide media ridicule.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMiles_and_Badman20031969:_.22They_were_ridiculed_by_the_world.27s_media.22_187-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMiles_and_Badman20031969:_.22They_were_ridiculed_by_the_world.27s_media.22-187"><span>[</span>187<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAnderson201083:_.22The_Bed-In_stunt_was_ridiculed_by_the_press.22_188-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAnderson201083:_.22The_Bed-In_stunt_was_ridiculed_by_the_press.22-188"><span>[</span>188<span>]</span></a></sup> At a second Bed-In three months later at the Queen Elizabeth Hotel in Montreal<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry2000b745.E2.80.93748_189-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry2000b745.E2.80.93748-189"><span>[</span>189<span>]</span></a></sup> Lennon wrote and recorded "Give Peace a Chance". Released as a single, it was quickly taken up as an anti-war anthem and sung by a quarter of a million demonstrators against the <a href="/wiki/Vietnam_War" title="Vietnam War">Vietnam War</a> in Washington, DC, on 15 November, the second <a href="/wiki/Moratorium_to_End_the_War_in_Vietnam" title="Moratorium to End the War in Vietnam">Vietnam Moratorium Day</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPerone200157.E2.80.9358_78-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPerone200157.E2.80.9358-78"><span>[</span>78<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHolsinger1999389_190-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHolsinger1999389-190"><span>[</span>190<span>]</span></a></sup> In December, they paid for billboards in 10 cities around the world which declared, in the national language, "War Is Over! If You Want It".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-191"><a href="#cite_note-191"><span>[</span>191<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Later that year, Lennon and Ono supported efforts by the family of <a href="/wiki/James_Hanratty" title="James Hanratty">James Hanratty</a>, hanged for murder in 1962, to prove his innocence.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWenner200043_192-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWenner200043-192"><span>[</span>192<span>]</span></a></sup> Those who had condemned Hanratty were, according to Lennon, "the same people who are running guns to South Africa and killing blacks in the streets. ... The same bastards are in control, the same people are running everything, it's the whole bullshit bourgeois scene."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEClark2002_193-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEClark2002-193"><span>[</span>193<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources#What_information_to_include" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources"><span title="A more detailed citation is required. (December 2014)">full citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> In London, Lennon and Ono staged a "Britain Murdered Hanratty" banner march and a "Silent Protest For James Hanratty",<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMiles_and_Badman2003_80-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMiles_and_Badman2003-80"><span>[</span>80<span>]</span></a></sup> and produced a 40-minute documentary on the case. At an <a href="/wiki/Court_of_Appeal_of_England_and_Wales" title="Court of Appeal of England and Wales">appeal hearing</a> years later, Hanratty's conviction was upheld<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMilmo2002_194-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMilmo2002-194"><span>[</span>194<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources#What_information_to_include" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources"><span title="A more detailed citation is required. (December 2014)">full citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> after <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/DNA_evidence" title="DNA evidence">DNA evidence</a> matched.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-195"><a href="#cite_note-195"><span>[</span>195<span>]</span></a></sup> His family continued to appeal in 2010.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-196"><a href="#cite_note-196"><span>[</span>196<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Lennon and Ono showed their solidarity with the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Clydeside" title="Clydeside">Clydeside</a> <a href="/wiki/Upper_Clyde_Shipbuilders" title="Upper Clyde Shipbuilders">UCS</a> workers' <a href="/wiki/Work-in" title="Work-in">work-in</a> of 1971 by sending a bouquet of red roses and a cheque for £5,000.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcGinty2010_197-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcGinty2010-197"><span>[</span>197<span>]</span></a></sup> On moving to New York City in August that year, they befriended two of the <a href="/wiki/Chicago_Seven" title="Chicago Seven">Chicago Seven</a>, <a href="/wiki/Youth_International_Party" title="Youth International Party">Yippie</a> peace activists <a href="/wiki/Jerry_Rubin" title="Jerry Rubin">Jerry Rubin</a> and <a href="/wiki/Abbie_Hoffman" title="Abbie Hoffman">Abbie Hoffman</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry2000b344_198-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry2000b344-198"><span>[</span>198<span>]</span></a></sup> Another political activist, <a href="/wiki/John_Sinclair_(poet)" title="John Sinclair (poet)">John Sinclair</a>, poet and co-founder of the <a href="/wiki/White_Panther_Party" title="White Panther Party">White Panther Party</a>, was serving ten years in prison for selling two <a href="/wiki/Joint_(cannabis)" title="Joint (cannabis)">joints</a> of marijuana after previous convictions for possession of the drug.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBuchanan2009_199-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBuchanan2009-199"><span>[</span>199<span>]</span></a></sup> In December 1971 at <a href="/wiki/Ann_Arbor,_Michigan" title="Ann Arbor, Michigan">Ann Arbor, Michigan</a>, 15,000 people attended the "<a href="/wiki/John_Sinclair_Freedom_Rally" title="John Sinclair Freedom Rally">John Sinclair Freedom Rally</a>", a protest and benefit concert with contributions from Lennon, <a href="/wiki/Stevie_Wonder" title="Stevie Wonder">Stevie Wonder</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bob_Seger" title="Bob Seger">Bob Seger</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bobby_Seale" title="Bobby Seale">Bobby Seale</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Black_Panther_Party" title="Black Panther Party">Black Panther Party</a>, and others.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry2000b789.E2.80.93790.2C_812.E2.80.93813_200-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry2000b789.E2.80.93790.2C_812.E2.80.93813-200"><span>[</span>200<span>]</span></a></sup> Lennon and Ono, backed by <a href="/wiki/David_Peel_(musician)" title="David Peel (musician)">David Peel</a> and Rubin, performed an acoustic set of four songs from their forthcoming <i>Some Time in New York City</i> album including "John Sinclair", whose lyrics called for his release. The day before the rally, the <a href="/wiki/Michigan_Senate" title="Michigan Senate">Michigan Senate</a> passed a bill that significantly reduced the penalties for possession of marijuana and four days later Sinclair was released on an appeal bond.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGlenn2009_201-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGlenn2009-201"><span>[</span>201<span>]</span></a></sup> The performance was recorded and two of the tracks later appeared on <i><a href="/wiki/John_Lennon_Anthology" title="John Lennon Anthology">John Lennon Anthology</a></i> (1998).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECalkin2002_202-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECalkin2002-202"><span>[</span>202<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Following the <i><a href="/wiki/Bloody_Sunday_(1972)" title="Bloody Sunday (1972)">Bloody Sunday</a></i> incident in <a href="/wiki/Northern_Ireland" title="Northern Ireland">Northern Ireland</a> in 1972, in which 14 unarmed <a href="/wiki/Northern_Ireland_Civil_Rights_Association" title="Northern Ireland Civil Rights Association">civil rights protesters</a> were shot dead by the British Army, Lennon said that given the choice between the army and the <a href="/wiki/Official_Irish_Republican_Army" title="Official Irish Republican Army">IRA</a> (who were not involved in the incident) he would side with the latter. Lennon and Ono wrote two songs protesting British presence and actions in Ireland for their <i>Some Time in New York City</i> album: "Luck of the Irish" and "Sunday Bloody Sunday". In 2000, <a href="/wiki/David_Shayler" title="David Shayler">David Shayler</a>, a former member of Britain's domestic security service MI5, suggested that Lennon had given money to the IRA, though this was swiftly denied by Ono.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBright2000_203-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBright2000-203"><span>[</span>203<span>]</span></a></sup> Biographer Bill Harry records that following Bloody Sunday, Lennon and Ono financially supported the production of the film <i>The Irish Tapes</i>, a political documentary with a <a href="/wiki/Irish_republicanism" title="Irish republicanism">Republican</a> slant.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry2000b403_204-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry2000b403-204"><span>[</span>204<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>According to FBI surveillance reports (and confirmed by <a href="/wiki/Tariq_Ali" title="Tariq Ali">Tariq Ali</a> in 2006) Lennon was sympathetic to the <a href="/wiki/International_Marxist_Group" title="International Marxist Group">International Marxist Group</a>, a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Trotskyist" title="Trotskyist">Trotskyist</a> group formed in Britain in 1968.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAli2006_205-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAli2006-205"><span>[</span>205<span>]</span></a></sup> However, the FBI considered Lennon to have limited effectiveness as a revolutionary since he was "constantly under the influence of narcotics".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBrooks2005_206-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBrooks2005-206"><span>[</span>206<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In 1973, Lennon contributed a limerick called "Why Make It Sad To Be Gay?" to Len Richmond's <i>The Gay Liberation Book</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-207"><a href="#cite_note-207"><span>[</span>207<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Lennon's last act of political activism was a statement in support of the striking minority sanitation workers in San Francisco on 5 December 1980. He and Ono planned to join the workers' protest on 14 December.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-208"><a href="#cite_note-208"><span>[</span>208<span>]</span></a></sup> By this time, however, Lennon had also quietly renounced the counterculture views which he had helped promote during the 1960s and 1970s and became more aligned with <a href="/wiki/Conservatism" title="Conservatism">conservatism</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-209"><a href="#cite_note-209"><span>[</span>209<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-210"><a href="#cite_note-210"><span>[</span>210<span>]</span></a></sup> though whether he had actually aligned to a more conservative world view is disputed<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-211"><a href="#cite_note-211"><span>[</span>211<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Deportation_attempt">Deportation attempt</span></h3>
<p>Following the impact of "Give Peace a Chance" and "<a href="/wiki/Happy_Xmas_(War_Is_Over)" title="Happy Xmas (War Is Over)">Happy Xmas (War Is Over)</a>", both strongly associated with the anti–Vietnam War movement, the Nixon administration, hearing rumours of Lennon's involvement in a concert to be held in San Diego at the same time as the <a href="/wiki/Republican_National_Convention" title="Republican National Convention">Republican National Convention</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWiener19992_212-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWiener19992-212"><span>[</span>212<span>]</span></a></sup> tried to have him deported. Nixon believed that Lennon's anti-war activities could cost him his re-election;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBBC_News2000_213-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBBC_News2000-213"><span>[</span>213<span>]</span></a></sup> Republican Senator <a href="/wiki/Strom_Thurmond" title="Strom Thurmond">Strom Thurmond</a> suggested in a February 1972 memo that "deportation would be a strategic counter-measure" against Lennon.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWiener1990225_214-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWiener1990225-214"><span>[</span>214<span>]</span></a></sup> The next month the United States <a href="/wiki/Immigration_and_Naturalization_Service" title="Immigration and Naturalization Service">Immigration and Naturalization Service</a> (INS) began deportation proceedings, arguing that his 1968 misdemeanor conviction for cannabis possession in London had made him ineligible for admission to the United States. Lennon spent the next three and a half years in and out of deportation hearings until 8 October 1975, when a court of appeals barred the deportation attempt, stating "... the courts will not condone selective deportation based upon secret political grounds."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEColeman1992576.E2.80.93583_215-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEColeman1992576.E2.80.93583-215"><span>[</span>215<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBBC_News2006a_106-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBBC_News2006a-106"><span>[</span>106<span>]</span></a></sup> While the legal battle continued, Lennon attended rallies and made television appearances. Lennon and Ono co-hosted <i><a href="/wiki/The_Mike_Douglas_Show" title="The Mike Douglas Show">The Mike Douglas Show</a></i> for a week in February 1972, introducing guests such as <a href="/wiki/Jerry_Rubin" title="Jerry Rubin">Jerry Rubin</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bobby_Seale" title="Bobby Seale">Bobby Seale</a> to mid-America.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBBC_News2006c_216-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBBC_News2006c-216"><span>[</span>216<span>]</span></a></sup> In 1972, <a href="/wiki/Bob_Dylan" title="Bob Dylan">Bob Dylan</a> wrote a letter to the INS defending Lennon, stating:</p>
<blockquote>
<p>John and Yoko add a great voice and drive to the country's so-called art institution. They inspire and transcend and stimulate and by doing so, only help others to see pure light and in doing that, put an end to this dull taste of petty commercialism which is being passed off as Artist Art by the overpowering mass media. Hurray for John and Yoko. Let them stay and live here and breathe. The country's got plenty of room and space. Let John and Yoko stay!<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-217"><a href="#cite_note-217"><span>[</span>217<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-218"><a href="#cite_note-218"><span>[</span>218<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
</blockquote>
<p>On 23 March 1973, Lennon was ordered to leave the US within 60 days.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWiener1999326_219-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWiener1999326-219"><span>[</span>219<span>]</span></a></sup> Ono, meanwhile, was granted permanent residence. In response, Lennon and Ono held a press conference on 1 April 1973 at the <a href="/wiki/New_York_City_Bar_Association" title="New York City Bar Association">New York City Bar Association</a>, where they announced the formation of the state of <a href="/wiki/Nutopia" title="Nutopia">Nutopia</a>; a place with "no land, no boundaries, no passports, only people".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry2000b663_220-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry2000b663-220"><span>[</span>220<span>]</span></a></sup> Waving the white flag of Nutopia (two handkerchiefs), they asked for political asylum in the US. The press conference was filmed, and would later appear in the 2006 documentary <i><a href="/wiki/The_U.S._vs._John_Lennon" title="The U.S. vs. John Lennon">The U.S. vs. John Lennon</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEUrishBielen2007143_221-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEUrishBielen2007143-221"><span>[</span>221<span>]</span></a></sup> Lennon's <i><a href="/wiki/Mind_Games_(John_Lennon_album)" title="Mind Games (John Lennon album)">Mind Games</a></i> (1973) included the track "Nutopian International Anthem", which comprised three seconds of silence.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry2000b664_222-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry2000b664-222"><span>[</span>222<span>]</span></a></sup> Soon after the press conference, Nixon's involvement in a political scandal came to light, and in June the <a href="/wiki/Watergate_scandal" title="Watergate scandal">Watergate</a> hearings began in Washington, DC. They led to the president's resignation 14 months later. Nixon's successor, <a href="/wiki/Gerald_Ford" title="Gerald Ford">Gerald Ford</a>, showed little interest in continuing the battle against Lennon, and the deportation order was overturned in 1975. The following year, his US immigration status finally resolved, Lennon received his <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/United_States_Permanent_Resident_Card" title="United States Permanent Resident Card">"green card"</a> certifying his <a href="/wiki/Permanent_residency" title="Permanent residency">permanent residency</a>, and when <a href="/wiki/Jimmy_Carter" title="Jimmy Carter">Jimmy Carter</a> was inaugurated as president in January 1977, Lennon and Ono attended the Inaugural Ball.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEColeman1984a289_223-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEColeman1984a289-223"><span>[</span>223<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="FBI_surveillance_and_declassified_documents">FBI surveillance and declassified documents</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote boilerplate further">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Jon_Wiener#Wiener_and_the_Lennon_FBI_Files" title="Jon Wiener">Wiener and the Lennon FBI Files</a> under <a href="/wiki/Jon_Wiener" title="Jon Wiener">Jon Wiener</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Lennon_FBI_Files_after_ny19p1.jpg"><img alt="Document with portions of text blacked out, dated 1972." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="790" data-file-width="610" height="285" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Lennon_FBI_Files_after_ny19p1.jpg/220px-Lennon_FBI_Files_after_ny19p1.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Lennon_FBI_Files_after_ny19p1.jpg/330px-Lennon_FBI_Files_after_ny19p1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Lennon_FBI_Files_after_ny19p1.jpg/440px-Lennon_FBI_Files_after_ny19p1.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Lennon_FBI_Files_after_ny19p1.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Confidential (here declassified and censored) letter by <a href="/wiki/J._Edgar_Hoover" title="J. Edgar Hoover">J. Edgar Hoover</a> about FBI surveillance of John Lennon.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>After Lennon's death, historian <a href="/wiki/Jon_Wiener" title="Jon Wiener">Jon Wiener</a> filed a <a href="/wiki/Freedom_of_Information_Act_(United_States)" title="Freedom of Information Act (United States)">Freedom of Information Act</a> request for <a href="/wiki/Federal_Bureau_of_Investigation" title="Federal Bureau of Investigation">FBI</a> files documenting the Bureau's role in the deportation attempt.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWiener199913_224-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWiener199913-224"><span>[</span>224<span>]</span></a></sup> The FBI admitted it had 281 pages of files on Lennon, but refused to release most of them on the grounds that they contained national security information. In 1983, Wiener sued the FBI with the help of the <a href="/wiki/American_Civil_Liberties_Union" title="American Civil Liberties Union">American Civil Liberties Union</a> of <a href="/wiki/Southern_California" title="Southern California">Southern California</a>. It took 14 years of litigation to force the FBI to release the withheld pages.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFriedman2005252_225-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFriedman2005252-225"><span>[</span>225<span>]</span></a></sup> The ACLU, representing Wiener, won a favourable decision in their suit against the FBI in the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Court_of_Appeals_for_the_Ninth_Circuit" title="United States Court of Appeals for the Ninth Circuit">Ninth Circuit</a> in 1991.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWiener1999315_226-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWiener1999315-226"><span>[</span>226<span>]</span></a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_Justice" title="United States Department of Justice">Justice Department</a> appealed the decision to the <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Court_of_the_United_States" title="Supreme Court of the United States">Supreme Court</a> in April 1992, but the court declined to review the case.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWiener199952.E2.80.9354.2C_76_227-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWiener199952.E2.80.9354.2C_76-227"><span>[</span>227<span>]</span></a></sup> In 1997, respecting President <a href="/wiki/Bill_Clinton" title="Bill Clinton">Bill Clinton</a>'s newly instigated rule that documents should be withheld only if releasing them would involve "foreseeable harm", the Justice Department settled most of the outstanding issues outside court by releasing all but 10 of the contested documents.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWiener199952.E2.80.9354.2C_76_227-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWiener199952.E2.80.9354.2C_76-227"><span>[</span>227<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Wiener published the results of his 14-year campaign in January 2000. <i>Gimme Some Truth: The John Lennon FBI Files</i> contained facsimiles of the documents, including "lengthy reports by confidential informants detailing the daily lives of anti-war activists, memos to the White House, transcripts of TV shows on which Lennon appeared, and a proposal that Lennon be arrested by local police on drug charges".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWiener199927_228-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWiener199927-228"><span>[</span>228<span>]</span></a></sup> The story is told in the documentary <i>The U.S. vs. John Lennon</i>. The final 10 documents in Lennon's FBI file, which reported on his ties with London anti-war activists in 1971 and had been withheld as containing "national security information provided by a foreign government under an explicit promise of confidentiality", were released in December 2006. They contained no indication that the British government had regarded Lennon as a serious threat; one example of the released material was a report that two prominent British leftists had hoped Lennon would finance a left-wing bookshop and reading room.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEThe_Associated_Press2006_229-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEThe_Associated_Press2006-229"><span>[</span>229<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Writing_and_art">Writing and art</span></h2>
<p>Beatles biographer Bill Harry writes that Lennon began drawing and writing creatively at an early age with the encouragement of his uncle. He collected his stories, poetry, cartoons and caricatures in a Quarry Bank High School exercise book that he called the <i>Daily Howl</i>. The drawings were often of crippled people, and the writings satirical, and throughout the book was an abundance of wordplay. According to classmate Bill Turner, Lennon created the <i>Daily Howl</i> to amuse his best friend and later Quarrymen bandmate <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pete_Shotton" title="Pete Shotton">Pete Shotton</a>, to whom he would show his work before he let anyone else see it. Turner said that Lennon "had an obsession for <a href="/wiki/Wigan_Pier" title="Wigan Pier">Wigan Pier</a>. It kept cropping up", and in Lennon's story <i>A Carrot in a Potato Mine</i>, "the mine was at the end of Wigan Pier." Turner described how one of Lennon's cartoons depicted a bus stop sign annotated with the question, "Why?". Above was a flying pancake, and below, "a blind man wearing glasses leading along a blind dog—also wearing glasses".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry2000b179.E2.80.93181_230-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry2000b179.E2.80.93181-230"><span>[</span>230<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Lennon's love of wordplay and nonsense with a twist found a wider audience when he was 24. Harry writes that <i><a href="/wiki/In_His_Own_Write" title="In His Own Write">In His Own Write</a></i> (1964) was published after "Some journalist who was hanging around the Beatles came to me and I ended up showing him the stuff. They said, 'Write a book' and that's how the first one came about". Like the <i>Daily Howl</i> it contained a mix of formats including short stories, poetry, plays and drawings. One story, "Good Dog Nigel", tells the tale of "a happy dog, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Raised-leg_urination" title="Raised-leg urination">urinating on a lamp post</a>, barking, wagging his tail—until he suddenly hears a message that he will be killed at three o'clock". <i><a href="/wiki/The_Times_Literary_Supplement" title="The Times Literary Supplement">The Times Literary Supplement</a></i> considered the poems and stories "remarkable ... also very funny ... the nonsense runs on, words and images prompting one another in a chain of pure fantasy". <i>Book Week</i> reported, "This is nonsense writing, but one has only to review the <a href="/wiki/Literary_nonsense" title="Literary nonsense">literature of nonsense</a> to see how well Lennon has brought it off. While some of his homonyms are gratuitous word play, many others have not only double meaning but a double edge." Lennon was not only surprised by the positive reception, but that the book was reviewed at all, and suggested that readers "took the book more seriously than I did myself. It just began as a laugh for me".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry2000b393.E2.80.93394_231-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry2000b393.E2.80.93394-231"><span>[</span>231<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In combination with <i><a href="/wiki/A_Spaniard_in_the_Works" title="A Spaniard in the Works">A Spaniard in the Works</a></i> (1965), <i>In His Own Write</i> formed the basis of the stage play <i>The John Lennon Play: In His Own Write</i>, co-adapted by <a href="/wiki/Victor_Spinetti" title="Victor Spinetti">Victor Spinetti</a> and <a href="/wiki/Adrienne_Kennedy" title="Adrienne Kennedy">Adrienne Kennedy</a>. After negotiations between Lennon, Spinetti and the artistic director of the <a href="/wiki/Royal_National_Theatre" title="Royal National Theatre">National Theatre</a>, <a href="/wiki/Laurence_Olivier" title="Laurence Olivier">Sir Laurence Olivier</a>, the play opened at <a href="/wiki/The_Old_Vic" title="The Old Vic">The Old Vic</a> in 1968. Lennon and Ono attended the opening night performance, their second public appearance together.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry2000b396.E2.80.93397_232-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry2000b396.E2.80.93397-232"><span>[</span>232<span>]</span></a></sup> In 1969, Lennon wrote "Four in Hand"—a skit based on his teenaged experiences of <a href="/wiki/Circle_jerk_(sexual_practice)" title="Circle jerk (sexual practice)">group masturbation</a>—for <a href="/wiki/Kenneth_Tynan" title="Kenneth Tynan">Kenneth Tynan</a>'s play <i><a href="/wiki/Oh!_Calcutta!" title="Oh! Calcutta!">Oh! Calcutta!</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-233"><a href="#cite_note-233"><span>[</span>233<span>]</span></a></sup> After Lennon's death, further works were published, including <i><a href="/wiki/Skywriting_by_Word_of_Mouth" title="Skywriting by Word of Mouth">Skywriting by Word of Mouth</a></i> (1986); <i>Ai: Japan Through John Lennon's Eyes: A Personal Sketchbook</i> (1992), with Lennon's illustrations of the definitions of Japanese words; and <i>Real Love: The Drawings for Sean</i> (1999). <i><a href="/wiki/The_Beatles_Anthology" title="The Beatles Anthology">The Beatles Anthology</a></i> (2000) also presented examples of his writings and drawings.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Musicianship">Musicianship</span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Instruments_played">Instruments played</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote">Further information: <a href="/wiki/John_Lennon%27s_musical_instruments" title="John Lennon's musical instruments">John Lennon's musical instruments</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_the_Beatles%27_instruments" title="List of the Beatles' instruments">List of the Beatles' instruments</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:John_Lennon%27s_Les_Paul_Jr..jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1770" data-file-width="1565" height="192" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/John_Lennon%27s_Les_Paul_Jr..jpg/170px-John_Lennon%27s_Les_Paul_Jr..jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/John_Lennon%27s_Les_Paul_Jr..jpg/255px-John_Lennon%27s_Les_Paul_Jr..jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/John_Lennon%27s_Les_Paul_Jr..jpg/340px-John_Lennon%27s_Les_Paul_Jr..jpg 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:John_Lennon%27s_Les_Paul_Jr..jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Lennon's <a href="/wiki/Gibson_Les_Paul_Junior" title="Gibson Les Paul Junior">Les Paul Jr.</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Lennon's playing of a mouth organ during a bus journey to visit his cousin in Scotland caught the driver's ear. Impressed, the driver told Lennon of a harmonica he could have if he came to Edinburgh the following day, where one had been stored in the bus depot since a passenger left it on a bus.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry2000b313_234-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry2000b313-234"><span>[</span>234<span>]</span></a></sup> The professional instrument quickly replaced Lennon's toy. He would continue to play harmonica, often using the instrument during the Beatles' Hamburg years, and it became a signature sound in the group's early recordings. His mother taught him how to play the banjo, later buying him an acoustic guitar. At 16, he played rhythm guitar with the Quarrymen.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry2000b738.E2.80.93740_235-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry2000b738.E2.80.93740-235"><span>[</span>235<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>As his career progressed, he played a variety of electric guitars, predominantly the <a href="/wiki/Rickenbacker_325" title="Rickenbacker 325">Rickenbacker 325</a>, <a href="/wiki/Epiphone_Casino" title="Epiphone Casino">Epiphone Casino</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gibson_J-160E" title="Gibson J-160E">Gibson J-160E</a>, and, from the start of his solo career, the <a href="/wiki/Gibson_Les_Paul_Junior" title="Gibson Les Paul Junior">Gibson Les Paul Junior</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPrown_and_Newquist2003213_236-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPrown_and_Newquist2003213-236"><span>[</span>236<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELawrence200927_237-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELawrence200927-237"><span>[</span>237<span>]</span></a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Double_Fantasy" title="Double Fantasy">Double Fantasy</a></i> producer Jack Douglas claimed that since his Beatle days Lennon habitually tuned his D-string slightly flat, so his Aunt Mimi could tell which guitar was his on recordings.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-238"><a href="#cite_note-238"><span>[</span>238<span>]</span></a></sup> Occasionally he played a six-string bass guitar, the <a href="/wiki/Fender_Bass_VI" title="Fender Bass VI">Fender Bass VI</a>, providing bass on some Beatles numbers ("<a href="/wiki/Back_in_the_U.S.S.R." title="Back in the U.S.S.R.">Back in the U.S.S.R.</a>", "<a href="/wiki/The_Long_and_Winding_Road" title="The Long and Winding Road">The Long and Winding Road</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Helter_Skelter_(song)" title="Helter Skelter (song)">Helter Skelter"</a>) that occupied McCartney with another instrument.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEverett1999297_239-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEverett1999297-239"><span>[</span>239<span>]</span></a></sup> His other instrument of choice was the piano, on which he composed many songs, including "Imagine", described as his best-known solo work.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBlaney200583_240-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBlaney200583-240"><span>[</span>240<span>]</span></a></sup> His jamming on a piano with McCartney in 1963 led to the creation of the Beatles' first US number one, "<a href="/wiki/I_Want_to_Hold_Your_Hand" title="I Want to Hold Your Hand">I Want to Hold Your Hand</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEverett2001200_241-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEverett2001200-241"><span>[</span>241<span>]</span></a></sup> In 1964, he became one of the first British musicians to acquire a <a href="/wiki/Mellotron" title="Mellotron">Mellotron</a> keyboard, though it was not heard on a Beatles recording until "Strawberry Fields Forever" in 1967.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBabiuk2002164.E2.80.93165_242-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBabiuk2002164.E2.80.93165-242"><span>[</span>242<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Vocal_style">Vocal style</span></h3>
<p>When the Beatles recorded "<a href="/wiki/Twist_and_Shout" title="Twist and Shout">Twist and Shout</a>", the final track during the mammoth one-day session that produced the band's 1963 debut album, <i><a href="/wiki/Please_Please_Me" title="Please Please Me">Please Please Me</a></i>, Lennon's voice, already compromised by a cold, came close to giving out. Lennon said, "I couldn't sing the damn thing, I was just screaming."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWenner200014_243-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWenner200014-243"><span>[</span>243<span>]</span></a></sup> In the words of biographer Barry Miles, "Lennon simply shredded his vocal cords in the interests of rock 'n' roll."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMiles_and_Badman200390_244-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMiles_and_Badman200390-244"><span>[</span>244<span>]</span></a></sup> The Beatles' producer, <a href="/wiki/George_Martin" title="George Martin">George Martin</a>, tells how Lennon "had an inborn dislike of his own voice which I could never understand. He was always saying to me: 'DO something with my voice! ... put something on it ... Make it <i>different</i>.'"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEColeman1992369.E2.80.93370_245-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEColeman1992369.E2.80.93370-245"><span>[</span>245<span>]</span></a></sup> Martin obliged, often using <a href="/wiki/Double_tracking" title="Double tracking">double-tracking</a> and other techniques. Music critic Robert Christgau says that Lennon's "greatest vocal performance ... from scream to whine, is modulated electronically ... echoed, filtered, and double tracked."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWiener1990143_246-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWiener1990143-246"><span>[</span>246<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>As his Beatles era segued into his solo career, his singing voice found a widening range of expression. Biographer Chris Gregory writes of Lennon "tentatively beginning to expose his insecurities in a number of acoustic-led 'confessional' ballads, so beginning the process of 'public therapy' that will eventually culminate in the primal screams of "<a href="/wiki/Cold_Turkey" title="Cold Turkey">Cold Turkey</a>" and the cathartic <i><a href="/wiki/John_Lennon/Plastic_Ono_Band" title="John Lennon/Plastic Ono Band">John Lennon/Plastic Ono Band</a></i>."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGregory200775_247-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGregory200775-247"><span>[</span>247<span>]</span></a></sup> David Stuart Ryan notes Lennon's vocal delivery to range from "extreme vulnerability, sensitivity and even naivety" to a hard "rasping" style.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERyan1982118.2C_241_248-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERyan1982118.2C_241-248"><span>[</span>248<span>]</span></a></sup> Wiener too describes contrasts, saying the singer's voice can be "at first subdued; soon it almost cracks with despair".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWiener199035_249-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWiener199035-249"><span>[</span>249<span>]</span></a></sup> Music historian Ben Urish recalls hearing the Beatles' <i><a href="/wiki/The_Ed_Sullivan_Show" title="The Ed Sullivan Show">Ed Sullivan Show</a></i> performance of "<a href="/wiki/This_Boy" title="This Boy">This Boy</a>" played on the radio a few days after Lennon's murder: "As Lennon's vocals reached their peak ... it hurt too much to hear him scream with such anguish and emotion. But it was my emotions I heard in his voice. Just like I always had."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEUrishBielen2007123_250-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEUrishBielen2007123-250"><span>[</span>250<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Legacy">Legacy</span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:182px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Lennon_Statue,_Liverpool.jpg"><img alt="A statue depicting a young Lennon outside a brick building. Next to the statue are three windows, with two side-by-side above the lower, which bears signage advertising the Cavern pub." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2946" data-file-width="2460" height="216" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Lennon_Statue%2C_Liverpool.jpg/180px-Lennon_Statue%2C_Liverpool.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Lennon_Statue%2C_Liverpool.jpg/270px-Lennon_Statue%2C_Liverpool.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Lennon_Statue%2C_Liverpool.jpg/360px-Lennon_Statue%2C_Liverpool.jpg 2x" width="180"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Lennon_Statue,_Liverpool.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Statue outside the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cavern_Club" title="Cavern Club">Cavern Club</a>, Liverpool</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Music historians Schinder and Schwartz, writing of the transformation in popular music styles that took place between the 1950s and the 1960s, say that the Beatles' influence cannot be overstated: having "revolutionised the sound, style, and attitude of popular music and opened rock and roll's doors to a tidal wave of British rock acts", the group then "spent the rest of the 1960s expanding rock's stylistic frontiers".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESchinderSchwartz2007160_251-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESchinderSchwartz2007160-251"><span>[</span>251<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Liam_Gallagher" title="Liam Gallagher">Liam Gallagher</a>, his group <a href="/wiki/Oasis_(band)" title="Oasis (band)">Oasis</a> among the many who acknowledge the band's influence, identifies Lennon as a hero; in 1999 he named his first child Lennon Gallagher in tribute.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry2000b265_252-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry2000b265-252"><span>[</span>252<span>]</span></a></sup> On <a href="/wiki/National_Poetry_Month#International_Poetry_Celebrations" title="National Poetry Month">National Poetry Day</a> in 1999, after conducting a poll to identify the UK's favourite song lyric, the BBC announced "Imagine" the winner.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry2000b382.E2.80.93383_95-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry2000b382.E2.80.93383-95"><span>[</span>95<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In a 2006 <i><a href="/wiki/The_Guardian" title="The Guardian">Guardian</a></i> article, Jon Wiener wrote: "For young people in 1972, it was thrilling to see Lennon's courage in standing up to [US President] Nixon. That willingness to take risks with his career, and his life, is one reason why people still admire him today."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWiener2006_253-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWiener2006-253"><span>[</span>253<span>]</span></a></sup> For music historians Urish and Bielen, Lennon's most significant effort was "the self-portraits ... in his songs [which] spoke to, for, and about, the human condition."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEUrishBielen2007121.E2.80.93122_254-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEUrishBielen2007121.E2.80.93122-254"><span>[</span>254<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Lennon continues to be mourned throughout the world and has been the subject of <a href="/wiki/Death_of_John_Lennon#Memorials_and_tributes" title="Death of John Lennon">numerous memorials and tributes</a>.
